<Author>Myrts78
<Content>Felt Liike Royalty We just returned from a four night stay at the Royal Hawaiian and it was lovely. After reading some very negative reviews we were very apprenhensive about staying there however our fears were unfounded. From the moment we stepped into the hotel and saw the granduer of the lobby and the magnificience we were in awe. It was truly a step back in time to old elegance and palatial beauty not gawdy just exquisite. The fault is with the rooms, somewhat dated. Our first offered garden view room was OK but not special so we upgraded to a tower oceanview room at a cost of $100.extra per night and was told it was a special price. The tower is the newer part of the hotel and therefore nicer, the astounding panaroma view of Waikiki beach was worth the money!!!!! Room # 1008. The only problem was that the balcony railing seemed too low and I felt uncomfortable standing too close to the edge. The birds hang out on the railings looking for scraps and therefore leave some droppings.The rest of the hotel is unsurpassed in old world elegance and charm, the beach is wonderful and you can walk out very far in the water and it is not deep. Some spots have a bit of coral so if you think you need it wear water shoes. Also the Luau is very nice my first one so nothing to compare, the food was good not fantastic, the show is great and if you are a guest of RH or Sheraton you get a 20% of automatically, it cost around 96.00 regularly. Barbara Eden was at ours with her husband he is a builder and apparently had something to do with the Sheraton. I highly recommend the Majestic Island tour if you have not seen the island before you will be surprised at the beauty of Oahu, there are things you cannot see by bus or shuttle, well worh it. The concierge at RH arranges everything for you and answers all your questions. We loved the hotel even in it's pre -repaired state so we can only imagine how it will be after.

<Content>Looking forward to returning after remodel I spent a week here recently, early May. I was traveling with my young two year old son. 1. We were upgraded to a huge suite. I called security for assistance and proceeded to lose my mind whilst running up and down the halls of each floor calling for him. 4. The furniture was spotless, not chipped, stained, broken, etc. The bathroom was clean, no mildew/mold. 5. Housekeeping was friendly and did an excellent job daily. 6. The food was okay, not great. I anxiously await the remodel, and hope that much of the staff returns to work at the refurbished property. I hear that a new pool area might be going in where the grassy luau area is now and that would be fabulous. We shall see!

<Author>TexasTX_Travelers
<Content>Classic Beauty in the heart of the action Booked a stay here with Amex Fine Hotels and Resorts program. We were a little concerned after reading some of the reviews but the concerns were almost completely unfounded. This resort is tucked away from the madness of Waikiki but still in the middle of it all. The grounds and the hotel itself are beautiful. It seems like it would be tough to find this type of setting anywhere else on Oahu. Heather Locklear was even there filming a movie in the Courtyard one day.The hotel lobby and common areas as well as the grounds, pool, and beach were very well maintained. The staff was superb - numerous and always friendly and willing to help. Our room had some delicous fresh baked bread in it when we arrived and after we came back from dinner we had a lovely gift basket with all sorts of treats waiting for us compliments of the hotel. We also had the breakfast buffet each morning, which sits right down next to the beach and is a fantastic setting.Our room was upgraded to an Oceanfront room. It was a large room with big lanai facing the beach and pool. Fantastic view. It had a comfortable bed and a flat panel TV. My only complaint is that it was billed as a recently renovated room. Other than the flat screen TV, not much looked recently renovated. There was some peeling wallpaper and some mold in the bathroom.We also did the luau on Monday night. This is a great experience. It is the only one in Waikiki and a lot of fun. They were terribly understaffed though and drinks were hard to come by. I think our waitress was probably helping 50 people.All in all a very fun time was had by my wife and I and we loved the classic charm and elegance of the Royal Hawaiian.

<Author>tlovestravel
<Content>Wonderful stay at Royal Hawaiian We used Hotwire (for the first time) to book 2 rooms and were surprised and excited that we were booked at the Royal Hawaiian. After reading some reviews from people booking online, using discount bookings like Hotwire, we were a little apprehensive about the service we would receive at the hotel. Before leaving for our trip, we inquired about a crib for the baby and were told that one would be available at no extra charge. We arrived and were greeted with flower leis and bead necklaces. At the check-in desk we asked about the crib and were told that it was already in the room. We also asked if we could upgrade one of the rooms to a larger room (we had 2 adults and 2 teens in our room with 2 double beds). We were given some options, but declined, as the upgrade cost was more than we had paid for the room originally. We were told that a larger room would be available in two days, at the same room rate, if we wanted to check back. After seeing the room 2 days later, we decided to switch - this room consisted of a large room with 2 double beds, and a large 'sitting room' with a fold-out bed; it did overlook part of the roof, but also provided a great ocean view. We actually couldn't believe that this room would be at the same rate as the first one, and thought that they may have just been trying to accomodate our request for more space. The service we received during our entire stay was exemplary - every need and request was promptly and courteously taken care of. When we asked if there were any more umbrellas available at the beach so we could bring the baby out, the attendant walked up and down the rows and found one that wasn't being used, then brought it to us and set it up. If this is typical of Royal Hawaiian service, we'll be back!

<Author>kimbermama
<Content>Not so good anymore This used to be spectacular so I was shocked at how low it's dropped. I wanted to write everyone here to tell you because I was disappointed and I always rely on this site for good tips. First off, just understand there are no lanais! Second, the beach--half the chairs are reserved (through a very mysterious process that is not even available to ocean front suite guests) so you have to rise by 5:30 a.m. to get one. People fight over them! You can't believe there's rat race there, but it's true. Then the chairs are all removed by 4 p.m.(This is Waikiki, towel-to-towel land, you need a beach chair!!) Just as you are enjoying the afternoon they come and tell you to go. That was very strange and discomfiting. Can you imagine a beach resort doing this? The food is bad--all fried fish sticky stuff flown in from the mainland and microwaved. We were all sick and had to find food elsewhere (the fab Matsugan two blocks away, where they make the noodles in front of you, marvelous!) Access to the beach from the main hotel lobby is closed off till 10 a.m. You have to go a round about way over to the tower to get out there. Or you can climb over the gate, which is what we did every morning (at 5 a.m.!!). The rooms are very old world charm -- they're okay if you like that sort of thing. Also, the crowd. They are much older. Much older! That was fine until our young family went over to the Mona Surfrider. It was gorgeous, lively, exciting--I sort of wished I had booked that. (Keep in mind, you do not go to Waikiki for solitude!)The hotel staff seems a grouchy unhappy bunch. We had a wonderful time in Waikiki despite all this (especially at the Moana's courtyard one night--beautiful!!!). Oh, and the pool. It sucks, no way around that. And the service? There isn't any to speak of. This is not the Four Seasons, I realize, but I expected more of the Royal Hawaiian. It is pretty and pink and very feminine. The carpets and lobby and ceilings are lovely! The shops are nice! But stay elsewhere if you want service and true luxury and a seat on the beach.

<Author>justsun
<Content>Changed for the worse... We are platinum members of the Starwood Preferred Guests program. Even with our status which is supposed to promise an upgrade to the best available room, we were still very disappointed.Let me start by saying we used to LOVE this hotel, and a few generations of our family have honeymooned there. We went there to celebrate a birthday and was our third time there....only to find that management has changed (they were bought out by a finance group from Asia).Our room was fine--the only thing that didn't change too much, although the products are worse quality than better (probably due to cost-cutting).Birthday Brunch was horrible. The waiters are imported from another country and not the typical warm locals that we were used to (again, probably another cost issue). One waiter walked with the fork and knife pointing outwards, and almost took my husband's eye out. Luckily my husband ducked the last minute and avoided tragedy. He stepped on my husband (wearing flip flops) subsequently and didn't even apologize! What kind of standard is that? I've had better service from 3rd world countries. It took forever to get our drinks while we were eating.The spa was expensive and not worth it. I paid a lot for a facial, and could have gotten the same one for half the price. They put away the becah chairs from the beach really early (i think it was 4PM), and we couldn't even sit there to enjoy the sunset! We asked why, and they said since management has changed, rules have also changed. The old timer staff apparently do not like new management, and many have left. Oh, and one more thing, I asked to use the restroom in the restaurant. Being pregnant, you would think they would be a little nicer. After being told no twice and going through two managers, they reluctantly opened up the restroom. How rude and inconsiderate, especially considering we are guests. All in all, they have changed and not for the better. We couldn't stand it and checked out a day early. Instead we went to the Sheraton Moana Surfrider (also another Starwood Property). We got much better treatment which is pathetic since Royal Hawaiian is supposed to be a luxury collection hotel (one step higher than the Sheraton). We're never going back again. Save your money and stay at the Sheraton instead...

<Content>Location, location, location!!!!! We stayed for a week in late January. There is no better location (though a couple may be equal). <Author>la femme folle
<Content>best location in Honolulu My husband, 2 year old son and I visited RH for 4 nights in January. I was a bit worried by some of the reviews of late. I know that the hotel is closing in a few months for the remainder of 2008, so I hope I can go back again after the make over. We didn't have any real problems though. We had a historic building ocean front room. The room was quite large with high ceiling and windows that open for the fresh air(there wasn't any bad smell in the room as some others have said). The TVs need to be replaced as they are quite out of date. There was coffee maker and a small refrigerator in the room and plenty of room for a crib. The bathroom was pretty standard and my only complaint were the bathroom amenities, ie shampoo etc, they were terrible! They need to upgrade those...Some staff were very accomodating and friendly, but we did find the restaurant servers did not seem to care about much. The food in the restaurants was nothing to write home about either. The food at the luau, like the pork and chicken dishes were very good and the show is very enjoyable.The best parts of the hotel are the mai tai bar (service there was always good and the live music was great), and the location. There is a ton of shopping within walking distance as well as the aquarium and the zoo. We mostly ate out since there are so many good restaurants around (Paradiso and Cheesecake Factory are right next door). The beach at the hotel is beautiful too! We are looking forward to coming back in 2009!

<Content>Lovely Place for Christmas The Pink Palace is a lovely place to stay for Christmas! The whole place is decorated beautifully. Every evening there is caroling in the lobby by various community groups.  If you want to enjoy the fabulous Christmas dinner, book early! Also, we had asked for a garden view room, higher floor, and had let the hotel know in advance that we were celebrating our 25th anniversary. We are also Starwood members. Yet, when we checked in we were told that they only had smoking rooms so we ended up with a low floor, driveway-view room which was a bit noisy . We expected better than this since we had booked well ahead, are Starwood members, and were celebrating a very special occasion. In our past travels, nearly every upscale hotel we have stayed in has done something (fruit basket, champagne, room upgrade, etc. ) for special occasions, but not this one. Still, it is a gorgeous place and I hope it retains its charm after the planned renovation.

<Author>tjtjtj
<Content>Great Location and Charm I was pleased to find the hotel tucked away from the hustle and bustle of Waikiki's main street. And you can't beat the beach location. The first room we had was a bit shabby (peeling wall paper, bugs in the bathroom) but the staff was helpful and accomodating in moving us to a better room. Self parking was $15 around the corner and provided some savings and pretty convenient for us traveling with a little one. This property will undergo an $80 million (approx.) renovation with about $60 mill going to the structure and $20 mill to update the rooms. Apparently there are plans for 3 pools and a waterslide in the current pool area (which is small, so it'll be interesting to see how they fit it all). Didn't eat at the hotel, but the menu looked pricey.

<Author>JohnnyCLosAngeles
<Content>Love it, Love it, Love it! While this may not be the newest or most modern hotel in Honolulu, it certainly has the most character and I mean that in a good way. Hotel rooms have the ability to be indistinguishable from each other, ie a decent bed, desk, internet cable, armoire and maybe a porch, but this has all that but with a style that transports you back in time to an era when travel to Hawaii was a luxury and it was truly a unique experience. Hotel services are excellent, staff is friendly, and its own roped-off beach is worth a lot when the beach otherwise fills up.Great discounts are available through Starwood whereby certain Starwood (ie Sheraton) restaurants are discounted, and this can make a difference in the cost of a stay.Oceanfront rooms have their own allure, but the larger rooms face the garden. This is because when travelers came to the hotel via steamship, many have had enough sun by the time the boat arrived, and the ones who opted for suites wanted them in the shade. So either side is desirable.

No one would use one of the bathrooms (we had two adjoining rooms) because it smelled. As parents, we just kind of ignored it to avoid a full scale protest. Would I stay here again, probably not.

<Author>mwooduk
<Content>Fell in love with The Pink Palace We stayed here for five nights for my husband's 50th birthday. I emailed the manager in advance ref: an upgraded room since it was a special occasion and we got it! Ocean front view of Waikiki and Diamondhead - it couldn't have been any better. Also pink champagne and homemade banana bread greeted us in our room! The room was gorgeous, all pink - plus lei's upon arrival. Bathroom was pink marble with the softest pink towels. Great amenities and coffee and frig in room - all replaced daily by delightful staff. Shower was a little old, but the hotel is old so it was to be expected but the immense charm outweighs any tiny inconveniences. The hotel will be closed from June 08- Dec. 08 for a complete renovation. I hope they don't take away it's charm and historical elements. It is a gorgeous hotel and was the second hotel ever to be built on Waikiki. Negatives - small pool and no exercise room or business center on site but we used both next door at the Sheraton Waikiki for a nominal charge. Perhaps this will change after the renovations next year? We had three treatments at the Abhasa Spa which was delightful - get a massage or a facial in the garden cabana with the sound of the bubbling water pot next to you - total relaxation guaranteed. Staff phenomenal.

<Content>Old Lady still has her charm We used a starwood promotion to book a suite. I think we got 50% off a 600$/suite. When we checked in, they put us in the new tower. It is fine, you are way up high, and the view is great, but it wasn't what we wanted. They then found a room in the old 3 story buidling. We stayed in a corner Jr. Suite on the 3rd floor. The bathroom is small but the room is huge and very quiet since you are on the corner: you have a view of waikiki and diamond head out the front and off to the side you can see the pool of the sheraton and the marina and pearl harbor in the distance. Right in front, there is a seperate beach area reserved for guests which is really great. You can wake up late and still not worry about finding a spot.The hotel exudes history and I urge you try a stay in one of the ocean facing rooms in the old building.

<Author>pattayainsider
<Content>Still very worthwhile Waikiki isn't what it was in the 1950's, but it's still fun for what it is. If you're expecting peace and quiet and space, like a 5 star deluxe hotel on one of the other islands, you'll be disappointed. If you like luxury, and fun and convenience and location, the Royal Hawaiian can't be beat. We had rooms in the new tower, ocean front, with the lanai. The lanai is critical. If you're staying in the old wing, there are no balcony's/lanais, and it's a total waste to me. The new tower rooms are a little small, but the views are the best in Waikiki. I repeat that it's a total waste to be on vacation in Hawaii and NOT have a nice balcony to use. The old building with no balconys is quite obsolete to me.The buffet breakfast was fine. We had light lunches by the pool, which were fine. The evening outdoor bar entertainment at sunset was nice on the beach. The maid service was fine, everything worked, no smell, no mold, no mildew in our rooms. Convenience is the most important thing here... you can walk to so many other great places to eat, just steps away, AND you're still on the beach. They had a 50% off rate, still over $300 a night, but worth it. ONe of our rooms had the 4 pm late checkout (we had a nightflight on departure), which was great to have the late checkout. They also offer a free community room for those without late checkout where you can relax, watch t.v., even take a shower before your flight. Nice shopping inside the hotel, grounds still beautiful, beach still nice, service still good. It's no longer 1950, but it's still a great place to vacation... lots going on, not boring. Some of the other luxury hotels on other islands are DEAD after 5 pm. The Royal Hawaiian isn't. Still highly recommended by me.

<Author>Tsukubaman
<Content>A Beautiful , old lady ... with dripping mascara I wanted to like staying here - I really did! But, in the end, it wasnot at all as charming as I thought it would be.Check-in was lovely as we were upgraded without having to ask for it.However, the suite we received was not quite what I imagined: 2end floor, old hotel, ocean front- sounds good, yeah?! Well ... it was and it wasn't. View-wise, it was lovely; as far as furniture and interior, it looked like a used dorm room. I realize the room turn-over in Hawaii is tremendous, especially at popular hotels, but surely a single night's fee would replace an entire sofa and/or a chair or two! Sparse, well-worn and without a designer's eye is how Iwould best describe it. The Bedroom area was better however, but carpeting, generally - throughout the hotel, needs a face-lift. I've read here that they are closing soon for a 7 month make-over. This should help - and lucky you who come after.: )The Seafood Buffet (Fri. only) was a surprisingly great value. The staff were friendly (but WHO isn't in Hawaii?!) and efficient. Recommended; even if you aren't staying there, though you need a reservation.The pool/ beach staff were all wonderful and the location is excellent for anything you want to do in Oahu. If, like me, you REALLY MUST stay here once, I'd probably ask for a better room and pay more were I to do it again. I really think it is a matter of Sheraton/Starwood not having enough money (nor wanting to spend it) to take good care of this grand old lady, and make it the first class place it is rumored to be. I realize it is an old hotel and an icon and that maintenance costs must be enormous, but I would say to Starwood, don't buy it if you can't afford to keep it up. Sadly, in Canada, the Fairmont group seems to be in the same straights with the old CP hotel group including such icons as the Banff Springs Hotel - now a 3 to 3.5 star experience in a 5 star hotel, supposedly - except in the most excellent rooms. I'm glad I had a chance to stay here, but would go to the Halekalani, easily, next time, which cost about the same and was up to expectations. :(As well, be careful of the 'welcoming' message from Starwood Hotels' located, conveniently, in the main lobby'. They want to sign you up for a 90 minute presentation on a time-share purchase plan on Kauaii they are building. They offer 'presents', but don't bother unless youare really interested in said purchase - enjoy Hawaii instead! BewareMainlanders bearing gifts ... ; )!

<Author>schnorrer
<Content>Charm and Class My wife and I stayed at this hotel on a recent 鈥渄elayed honeymoon鈥? It located on a very prime stretch of Waikiki beach with beautiful views of Diamond Head, surfers and outriggers, and is within easy walking distance to many good restaurants and shopping. The beach in front of the hotel is broad, without seawalls or jetties to get in the way, and there are few rocks or coral in the water to step on.The hotel is lovely to look at- it has a classic charm, with high archways, beautiful rugs and artwork, and gorgeous gardens with a variety of tropical plants. The hotel鈥檚 stucco-like surface and squarish shape makes it seem like a big sand castle that rose up from the beach! The pink color is not overwhelming, and complements the blue sky and blue water. Although this hotel is 鈥渃lassic鈥? the pastel pink color gives it a festive, fun vacation spirit. The lobby was quiet and grand, with little alcoves with wicker chairs and chaise lounges to relax in. Along the main lobby hallway are a few high-end shops, and it ends in an archway that opens onto a green lawn and then the beach and water beyond.Check-in was smooth and friendly- but we got there early and the room was not available until 2pm (check in time is 3pm). We were upgraded to an ocean-view room in the tower. Elevators were fast, the room was clean, no smell, it had a hi-def large TV, quiet and efficient air-conditioner, two phones and desk, large balcony with two chairs (鈥渓anai鈥?, modern bathroom, no mini-bar but the room had a good refrigerator, well-stocked coffee maker, free safe in the closet, internet for a fee, ironing board and iron in the closet, and free local newspaper each morning. The doors were card keyed. There were smoke detectors in each room. The swimming pool was smallish, somewhat old, but clean. The pool is located next to the beach, and very well heated. Cabanas were available, and plenty of chairs.We didn鈥檛 eat in the hotel restaurant for dinner, but had drinks at the outdoor Mai Tai bar, which had nightly Hawaiian music/light jazz entertainment and hula.Misc Tips:1) We searched very hard at the hotel鈥檚 website, and got a free breakfast package included. The breakfast buffet was excellent and extensive, but too expensive if not included in the room (so definitely get it as part of a room package). The Surf Room restaurant opens onto the beach and a great place to start the day.2) We originally reserved a room in the architecturally interesting original portion of the hotel, but accepted the tower for an ocean view upgrade. This worked out very well for us, as the tower elevators lead right out to the pool and beach. Since we spent our vacation days in our bathing suits and swimming, it was very convenient not to have to walk through the lobby with wet bathing suits! Also, the lanai with a view was a great escape from the midday sun, and a very relaxing place to have lunch.3) The hotel offers its guests a generous stretch of private beach, but get there early if you want a chaise lounge chair with an umbrella. (there were always plenty of lounge chairs, but the umbrellas went fast!)From reading other reviews, we had worried that this hotel had become a somewhat dated and worn-out 鈥淕rand Old Lady鈥?of the beach. Instead, we found the hotel beautiful, fresh, and charming. We would most definitely stay here again.

<Author>all4travel
<Content>Love Grand Old Hotels? The Royal Hawaiian is for you. My wife and I just returned from 5 fabulous nights at the Royal Hawaiian. If you love grand old hotels, then the Royal Hawaiian is for you. Yes, the rooms are smaller than some would expect. If you want large rooms, a larger pool, absolutely near perfect and up-to-date amenities and contemporary furniture then you would be better of at a newer hotel such as Hilton Hawaiian Village, Halekulani or Embassy Suites. This hotel exudes a warmth and grace from a time long gone. I hope it never changes.We stayed in the tower and were surprised how quiet the room was. We were directly across from the elevator and heard zero noise. There is construction throughout the area, again zero noise. Stay in the tower, spend the extra money and get a full ocean view with balcony. Go to their website and view images of every room style.The food, on the other hand, was a different story. We had the sea-food buffet and items that should be hot were lukewarm at best. Ditto with the breakfast buffet.We've stayed at the above mentioned hotels as well as the Hyatt Regency and Moana Surfrider. Would we stay at the Royal Hawaiian again? Absolutely! We'll just eat somewhere else or not get the buffet. Maybe we'll see you there at Christmas time!

<Author>worldtraveler80126
<Content>Lovely, Nostalgic hotel This is a wonderful nostalgic hotel; this pink palace was built in 1927. It is small, elegant, and situated right on the beach. For people who appreciate plants (all tropical), this is paradise. It is beautifully landscaped. The staff is very friendly and accomodating. There are many restaurants close to the hotel and lots of shopping as well. If you are looking for a huge hotel with lots of people and commotion, do not stay here. If you are looking for complete relaxation in an absolutely gorgeous atmosphere with a touch of nostalgia, this is your place. Having stayed in many hotels over the past years, it is hard to find one with quiet rooms. The rooms are very quiet at the RH. The Mai Tai Bar is real treat--great views of Waikiki Beach and Diamond Head and a variety of bands, most featuring Hawaiian music with hula dancers. On Friday nights, they offer a seafood dinner--this is worth the price and the view of the beach from the restaurant is fantastic. If you like sushi, they have a nice selection. All in all, my wife and I had a very nice time at the hotel and look forward to returning.

<Content>Lovely location but stay in the old part We stayed here for the first leg of our honeymoon.We had initially booked in to the Tower wing as some of the photos I had seen made the old part of the hotel look dated. However, when we arrived, I was pretty disgusted by the state of the room in the tower wing. It was dated, sparse and smelled really strongly of bleach. I thought the old part of the hotel was far more charming than the tower.You can't fault the location of this hotel, it's right on the beach and Waikiki is really beautiful, which sounds bizarre given that there are so many high rises. They have just refurbished it and it now looks very elegant and modern. They also have a Honolulu Coffee Company coffee shop actually in the hotel and you must try the Kona coffee. It is out of this world.The only other hotel I would consider would be Halekulani which I believe is really beautiful.I would definitely recommend Waikiki but do make sure you choose the right hotel.

<Author>norcal_dave
<Content>Worth the Hassle? I had my family of 5 in 2 connecting rooms in the older garden view section. We liked the rooms just fine - the beds were wonderful and the rest of the room amenities just average. As a previous review indicated, you do have to get to the beach VERY early if you want to get an umbrella - a strange thing in a luxury hotel. You'd think they could invest in more umbellas. The food at the restaurant was very average and overpriced. Dukes and Hula Grill next door were much better.The private beach advertised is separated from the public section by a small chain...so don't think private means secluded. But I think that is true for all hotels in Hawaii. Waikiki beach is a great family beach in that it is shallow for well over 100 yards out.The biggest issue we had was a severe mix up on our reservation and room rate. The Starwood reservation agent promised one thing and the hotel expected something very different, at a much higher price. To their credit, the hotel eventually delivered what was promised, at a slightly higher rate than promised, but it was only after much discussion - not a pleasant way to start a vacation.

<Author>LovedAventura
<Content>Royal Hawaiian NOT worh the price My husband and I visited Hawaii for two weeks in July and decided to stay at the Royal Hawaiian on our anniversary night. Let me start by saying that this hotel is definitely not worth the price you have to pay. We stayed in a tower room with an ocean front view. The room itself looked like an average hotel room just covered in pink (which I expected). Check-in took about 30 minutes. We told them during our booking that we were celebrating our 1-year anniversary night expecting a Happy Anniversary upon check-in or maybe even some fruit in our room upon arrival---well, I guess we expected too much. There was nothing complimentary at this hotel besides the small bread loaf that comes with every room. You have to pay $5 for the bottled water they put in your room and we didn't even get a chocolate on our pillow. For the price we paid (over $400 for one night) I expected at least a call checking in on us or in the very least free water. The beach was extremely crowded (as Waikiki is), the pool was very small and the hotel was nothing spectacular. I will most definitely not be staying there again. On the bright side though...the Mai Tai bar is great and the staff there were fantastic.

<Author>Keniston
<Content>Beach chairs top priority My husband and I stayed at the Royal Hawaiian for six nights in early July, 2007. We stayed in the historic section. The rooms were a bit dingy, but charming, too, with the abundance of pink linens. I loved the gardens and open lobbies, but do beware of birds roosting in light fixtures and side gutters. One nailed the glass table-top next to me, as I was waiting to check-out--something you just never get used to.I have two suggestions for improving a visit to this hotel.1) Travel books claim that the best mai-tai in town is at this hotel in the bar named after this cocktail. I ordered one right after I checked in. It was o.k., not sensational, and it was pricey, despite beautiful view. The next night I ordered one at the bar at Duke's, a short walk over, and it tasted better, cost less and the location still provided the same beautiful view. 2) Guests from the near-by hotels can charge food and snag pool deck-chairs and beach chairs and umbrellas, so you are competing with a large number of people everyday for prime spots. The fact that you are spending $300+ a night for your room does not guarantee you a space at the pool or beach. The first day I got there at 11 a.m. and there was not an umbrella available. The pool person suggest I go up to people who had umbrellas down and ask them if I could use them. Call me shy, but that method did not appeal to me. The next morning, I got to the beach at 7:45 a.m. I secured a couple chairs and then went back to the pool person to beg for an umbrella. He graciously set it up for me. I tipped him accordingly. Once I figured out the system, I was doing o.k., but I really don't want to work this hard on vacation. Next time I am choosing a place where I can just flop at the pool or beach anytime I want and not be worrying about the absolute basics of a summer vacation.  
<Date>Jul 27, 2007

<Author>wbdvldog
<Content>Don't like the Pink Lady, go home! We've stayed at the Royal Hawaiian roughly 12 times and each time we've experienced superb service. Yes, the historic wing needs refurbishment, especially the rooms, but this is the charm. The hotel was built in 1927. What do you expect? We absolutely love it and always get a spectacular room.My idea of a Hawaiian vacation is staying at the Royal, not renting a car or going on any day trips. Our days begin with a jog to Diamond Head and back, breakfast, the beach by 10 a.m., lunch/drinks at the Mai Tai Bar around 1, the beach, change over by 5, back down to the Mai Tai Bar for drinks and entertainment, finally, dinner around 8 and in bed by 9:30. The same process is repeated for the rest of the stay.From the first stay at the Royal we have been treated very well by everyone from the staff at the front desk to the housekeeping staff. I think people tend to forget that you are in Hawaii where the lifestyle is a little slower than LA, NY or Chicago. People, leave the attitude at home. The demanding ugly American attitude is very old, unpleasant and definitely unnecessary. I find it funny reading these posting that people who complain the most get treated the worst. You see the connection here? We are always greeted with great joy from everyone at the hotel. The wait staff at the Mai Tai Bar know us and know exactly what we want to drink from day one. Same rings true with the staff at the Surf Room. We always request the same waiter when we have dinner here. We were here during spring break in April and will be there again for a week on July 27th. We can't wait. Over the years we have met people who have been traveling there for over 25 years. We are meeting up with them again this year. We simply cannot wait. It's always sad leaving the Royal, but that's when the planning begins for the next visit.

Food service is good, the breakfast buffet is excellent but pricey. This hotel is a total ripoff (even for Hawaii) given the value for money you are getting Would not stay again.

<Author>HotelSnob2003
<Content>In the Pink at the Royal Hawaiian! We stayed at the RH for 3 nights in late June 2007 on the advice of friends who had stayed there in 2005. We booked a tower room and asked for a high floor, quiet area. We were given a 5th floor room at the end of the corridor. The room faced Waikiki west so we did not have a view Diamondhead, etc., but it sufficed.(At check-in, after a grueling 12-hour jaunt from the East Coast, the front desk said the computer was down' when I re-asked for a floor higher than the 5th.) Room was average, mattress was in need of revision, but the A/C and quiet worked well for us. Really, really loved the pink sheets and ultra-pink towels. Sunday breakfast buffet was nice, especially the refills of guava juice, and well, the view is to die for! Mai-tai bar service a little uneven, but who cares when you are sitting on the most famous beach in the world! We found all of the service folks in the bar and restaurant to be welcoming, albeit we had friendlier welcomes on the outer islands. Room service menu (after an exhausting day at Pearl Harbour and the Missouri) was average. We had a great meal at Duke's at the Outrigger next door (make reservations).(We asked to see a room in the historic section, and loved that too for future considerations.) RH is in a relatively quiet area, set back from the hubub of downtown Waikiki. Lotsa action on the beach side--luaus, wedding receptions, Outrigger Hotel singers etc.-- all part of the experience at staying in one of the premier spots on Waikiki. Overall, we loved the gardens, common areas:lobby lounges, etc. and the beach (sorry, I am guilty of nabbling some chairs early and using them all day). And the pink. We plan to return in 2009, and may make a week of the RH!

<Author>Cool_Aunt
<Content>Forego the Pink, cause it do STINK As seasoned travelers and frequent Hawaii visitors (we are the top level on both Hilton and Starwood, and Platinum on Hyatt) we have admittedly come to be quite demanding in our choice of hotels. But when you pay the big bucks for a well known, and almost revered Hawaiian hotel like the Pink Palace, you expect a little more...read on.We were told we were upgraded to an ocean view because of our Platinum starwood status. Although you could see the ocean, it was a poor view overlooking large green pipes in the foreground, and a small window (befitting the small room). The room was dinky, and shockingly dirty. This Sheraton was in one of the worst if not the worst conditions we have seen. The carpet was stained, the wallpaper was in disrepair, there were water stains by the air conditioning outlets, the bathroom had not been dusted. The shower was curtained, and was missing the normal curved out shower rod we have come to expect with the Starwood chain. While showering, you constantly were rubbed against by the wet shower curtain because the tub was so small. I wouldn't have dreamed of taking a bath because the room was so dirty.To be fair, the hallways and grounds are lovely and charming. The doors to the rooms are carved and gorgeous. But although we had booked a five-night stay, we checked out after one day and moved to the Hilton Hawaiian Village (which was heaven -- check out my review of this property if you want).We did complain about the room, but it was clear from the response of the front desk that they really didn't care. The employees and management of the revered Pink Palace have become complacent. Until they change their tune, our advice is STAY AWAY.

<Author>ottofred
<Content>the "Aloha Spirit" lives! I have just returned from a seven night stay (June 25-July 2, 2007) at The Royal Hawaiian Hotel on Waikiki Beach. I was traveling with a friend and we weren't looking for a slick and modern hotel with all the gadgets and amenities. Our preference is always for an old, well-established and maintained hotel with history, character and charm, and the Royal Hawaiian has all of this in abundance. But that's not all . . . this was our first visit to Hawaii and as newcomers we were anxious to experience Hawaiian culture and that additional feature that we understood to be the Aloha Spirit. From the moment we arrived, greeted by lei, smiling doormen, bellhops and gracious receptionists, we felt this spirit and, in fact, encountered it the entire week, not only at the hotel but in our travels around Oahu.The hotel itself is a magnificent, pink, moorish-inspired structure built in 1927 with an orginal section replete with ornate towers and interesting architectural details, and a later-built high rise addition.The lobbies, corridors and verandas are open and were evidently built to capture the trade winds, those fragrant cool breezes that wafted through the hotel on even the warmest days. All is lovely and gracious. Gorgeous tropical flower arrangements and numerous potted orchids are placed in hallways and corridors. Scores of diligent workers can be seen sweeping, vacumning, polishing, mopping and dusting, along with gardeners presiding over the lush array of tropical foliage on the extensive hotel grounds. Pick up a brochure in the concierge's office and take yourself on a self-guided tour of the hotel gardens as I did, and you will come away with an appreciation of the beauty, abundance, fragrances and variety of Hawaiian flora. I especially remember the intoxicating perfume of the gardenia trees that framed a doorway I passed through each morning on my way to breakfast in the Surf Room. Also on this pathway you can find bananas, bunches of them, still on the trees, Ti leaf plants and a potted pineapple plant.The Surf Room is one of the Royal Hawaiian hotel dining facilities overlooking Diamondhead and Waikiki Beach where you can have your choice of either continental, a la carte or buffet breakfast. The servers are warm and friendly and do their part to keep the Aloha Spirit alive. The only weak link in any of the Royal Hawaiian facilities was, in our opinion, the Mai Tai Bar, where, on repeated visits for drinks, snacks and entertainment, we had difficulty getting and maintaining the attention of the servers. However, that didn't detract from the beach front location and the seascape views of sand and aquamarine ocean, equally impressive at anytime of the day, from dawn to sunset and beyond. In fact, one afternoon a double rainbow appeared, framing Diamondhead and dipping into the whitecapped surf. As if the view wasn't enough!Our room was in the original hotel on the 5th floor with lovely views of lush gardens, waving palms and the high rise buildings of Honolulu, with a backdrop of beautiful racing cloud formations billowing over the mountains from the windward side of the island. The room was charming, traditionally furnished, well air-conditioned and quiet. Just as we like it. When we sunk down each night into the comfortable beds and pulled the silky pink sheets (embossed with the Royal Hawaiian signature moorish tower logo) up to our chins, all was well with the world.For us, as we will certainly return to Hawaii in the future, there will be no other place to stay but The Royal Hawaiian, with its casual yet elegant ambience, with not one iota of stuffiness. We believe that we experienced the Old Hawaii in all its charm and warmth, one of the reasons that Hawaiian culture intrigues and enchants travelers from around the world. The Royal Hawaiian has managed to capture and bestow this intangible element upon guests, which for me, in summary, is the Aloha Spirit.  
<Date>Jul 11, 2007

<Content>Dining not as good as it was We stayed at the Royal Hawaiian a few years ago and I must say I found it old fashioned but still a beautiful building.We enjoyed our evening meals overlooking Waikiki Beach as at that time they were very good indeed - this time they had gone downhill considerably which is a great shame. When we went we had to squeeze past building works to get to the hotel.There is a large brand new Sheraton a stones throw away which looks v.nice and, again, overlooks Waikiki Beach. As the Royal Hawaiin is a Starwood Hotel (Sheraton) we wondered whether they were not bothering anymore with the Royal Hawaiin ?

<Author>Clefsdorsf
<Content>Elegance and Charm in Waikiki The Royal has always been one of my favorite hotels. There are no fancy new TV's or iPod stations-- no hip lounge swith DJ music or stylish trendy decor. Instead--they have old world charm-- a staff full of the aloha spirit--and a spectacular beach front location that is the best in Waikiki. We enjoyed every moment of our stay-- and have already made a reservation to come back next year. We stayed in a suite in the historic building and loved the high ceilings and traditional decor. If you don't need the latest gagets in your room and like a bit of history in your hotel--you'll see why the Royal is the most famous hotel in Hawaii.

<Author>Gweede
<Content>Quaint but boring We stayed at RH for five nights in a historic room. I'm glad we got to experience this historic hotel but would have preferred to stay only one or two nights. There were no problems with our room or maid service, but felt the atmosphere was a bit dull and boring. After many days of getting up early to go off snorkleing or exploring. We like to go back our room and lounge for a while, get ready for dinner off-site, and then come back to hang out at the pool or bar. The tiny pool closed at 6:00 p.m. There is no hot tub at this hotel. They bring in all the lounge chairs off the beach also at 6:00 p.m., so the only way to enjoy the sunset is to sit at the outside bar but finding a good spot next to the beach is difficult. We would've enjoyed lounging on a chair on the beach and watching the stars alongwith the roaring waves. I asked why the chairs are removed so early, they said it was so those in the restaurant could enjoy the view of the ocean.This hotel is fine for older adults who like the quiet and who turn in after dinner. <Author>HUNDEN
<Content>Liked the pink palace Just got back from one week at Royal Hawaiian Hotel, Waikiki, stayed in the newer Tower. Everything went pretty smoothly and it was a pleasant stay except for a couple flaws:1. Upon arriving from a 5 1/2 hours flight from California, we arrived at Hotel at 11:00 a.m. because of our flight time landing, our room wasn't ready, no one mentioned the extra room lounge area, so we walked around Waikiki, killed time and got back to front desk 3:00 p.m. when they said room would be ready, room still not ready!, they said they were fully booked and had a staff shortage of maids!, solution Hire more maids!, then the lady told us to use the lounge on second floor for guests waiting, and gave us two free drink tickets for the bar, then around 5:00 p.m. our room was ready, we were so tired and jet lagged that we slept the whole time and missed Saturday night in Waikiki. 2. This incident only would be a reason for us to never use this Hotel again. 3. We have traveled to Hawaii many times and every hotel has given us our room early if we arrive early without us ever asking. The airlines and hotels should co-ordinate their flight times and hotel check in times since all people visiting Hawaii are flying in , except for the ones taking a 5 days cruise in, we cannot drive to Hawaii, and most people probably arrive from long flights prior to check in. If Hotel does not have enought maids, hire more maids! We talked to another couple whom had stayed here before and were staying here now and the same thing had happened to them. We are just afraid of checking into this hotel again and having to wait 5 hours to get our room.The food at the hotel restaurant was good. The Cabanas' by the pool were $75 a day plus tax of $3.00 approx. so that is $78approx. a day, they don't tell you about the tax until you sign up for the Cabana, it was easy to get a Cabana and pool chairs. They should take credit cards or cash for Cabana payment, get it set up, the beach desk only will charge it to your room, you sign a slip and they won't give you a copy of the slip, they should have an extra copy to give you. Pool water was warm. We went in off season before all the children got out of school. Buffet was good, but the indoor and outdoor restaurant had birds walking all over the floor and setting on empty tables with uncleared dishes eating out of the leftovers, ugh!!!!! Luau at Royal Hawaiian was good, if you are staying at Hotel you get $20 off per person for Luau, we booked Luau before we left California. We had an Ocean View room and it was clean, need more pictures on wall behind T.V. rather bland. Housekeeping was spotty. 3. It is a big rip-off that the hotel would charge you $20 a piece for the 2 Kuokooie Nut Necklaces they have in your room, (one in bathroom and one on bed, you put on bed to request sheet change) the high nightly price staying Royal Hawaiian would justify them giving you the Kuokooie Nut Necklace for free, or not having the necklace at all, we have gotten better and cheaper Kuokooie nut necklaces elsewhere. The Kaanapali Beach Hotel on Maui will give each person in your party a FREE Kuokooie nutshell necklace with a kiss and hug and Aloha upon departing. The Royal Hawaiian is in a good location near main drag. The above is a constructive criticism of the Hotel and as I said the Hotel and service was fine and nice the rest of the trip. 4. The service at the Pool. Well, the first day we were in a Cabana Bob or Rob an older gentleman worked his butt off giving excellent food and drink service walking up to everyone asking if they needed anything many times, very personable fellow. He is an excellent employee and deserves high praise. If you ever get his service give him a big tip, he is well worth it. Three days later a girl named Tina was the pool server, walked around carrying a menu, but rarely walked up to people asking to help, walked around a lot, she did ask us once if we needed anything and did bring us our food and water, but didn'[t come around a lot to see how we were doing. We had to walk up to her to get stuff later. She was pleasant but could have worked harder. We are not picky people and we are nice and patient and polite to everyone working there, and realize mistakes will be made. All in all the Royal Hawaiian is good. Very clean rooms great Ocean view. 5. The Royall Hawaiian Hotel concierge was not that helpful. We tried to book the Polynesian Cultural center through Royal Hawaiian Hotel's Concierge, she said on Monday the Polynesian Cultural center was closed so she couldn't get us tickets, she couldn't get us a rent a car, etc. We walked right over to Outrigger to Pleasant Hawaiian Holiday desk and they called and booked on Computer Polynesian Cultural center tour and rent a car right then and there. Concierge at Royal Hawaiian should have ability to book on computer Polynesian Cultural center.6. Polynesian Cultural center is an all day affair. It was grueling. They have you do a lot of walking, many elderly people on visit. The first canoe ride through the villages was bland. Expecting dancers and colorful uniforms in front of each village, had people partiipate in games that could have been skipped. It would have been better to just go for Nice IMAX theater movie and lovely evening show only. The buffet of beef and crab was so, so, waitress didn't clear tables often enough, we cleared our own. Food so so. Went on Dinner sunset cruise, booked through Pleasant Holidays desk, was nice. 7. Elevator near pool in new tower at Royal Hawaiian when coming in from pool area and facing elevators the elevator on far right will automatically default to Floor 14 every time you take elevator, no one pushing button on Floor 14, we always went to our room which was several floors below Floor 14, after many times this default to Floor 14 was annoying and time wasting. Glitch. Hope this review was helpful, and would recommend everyone try Royal Hawaiian Hotel at least once.

<Content>We loved it! We just returned from a fabulous week at the Royal Hawaiian. I wanted the hawaiian experience with all the fun stuff of Waikiki beach and that was exactly what we got.First of all, we booked the least expensive room (garden room) and they put us on the fourth floor of the original building overlooking the pool and beach...fabulous views. The room was good sized with huge ceilings and average bath, walk in closet, gorgeous floral wallpaper and king sized comfy bed. Like being in a bed and breakfast,. The gardens of the hotel were serene and relaxing to return to after spending the day shopping (minutes away) or on the beach. Lets face it, there are crowds at Waikiki beach and on the street, and the Hotel and its gardens were perfect after all the crazy people.Mai Tai bar was fun, we ate there at least five times. My husband surfed right off the shore and had a great time.We also ate at Dukes and Chucks right next door and both experiences were great.I am not sure what all the complaining about this place is, because we were there during the Don Ho memorial (20,000 people on the beach) and still had a fabulous time at the Royal Hawaiian Hotel...and definately will be back!

<Content>Loved the Royal Hawaiian! Just returned from Honolulu where I spent a night at the Royal Hawaiian! What a great place. And what history!TripAdvisor is an amazing site because it has really helped me to make some decisions on where to stay....and where not to stay. At least it was clean. Very clean. And very comfortable.If you want a brand spankin' new hotel, stay at one of the many modern palaces lining Waikiki. There are certainly plenty of them.The Royal Hawaiian was very stylish, and it was a pleasure staying there.When I research hotels, it doesn't take much time to realize which hotels are new, and which aren't. I knew of the history of the Royal Hawaiian, but even if I hadn't, it wouldn't have taken me long to figure out it's an old hotel. And with those years of longevity come the inevitable structural aging as well.Despite its age, it was a pure joy! Was it expensive? Yep. But worth the experience in my opinion.

<Author>soonerfans
<Content>Charming hotel on Waikiki We stayed at the Royal Hawaiian for 2 nights (April 15 and 16) and were very pleased. We chose it because it seemed so Hawaiian. If you like old buildings and architecture, you'll like this hotel. It's very charming, but if you're in the original building, remember, it's old. Don't expect it to be like the new high rises. When we arrived we were greeting very warmly with leis and had champagne waiting for us in our room (it was our 10th anniversary) along with banana nut bread (yum!). We were in room 558 which was a garden view but at the end of the hall. This was the quietest hotel room I've every stayed in. The room was small but clean and comfortable. The pool is also small but considering how crowded everything is, it's not surprising. The views of Diamond Head were wonderful. I felt like I was living in a post card. While in Honolulu we took a Roberts Hawaii tour to Pearl Harbor and then a short drive through the city. Pearl Harbor is amazing, but go early! We left the hotel at 6:30 AM. We want to take our kids there when they're older and can appreciate what they're seeing.Waikiki is very crowded. If you're looking for a quiet, relaxing, get-away... don't go to Waikiki. After 2 days, we went to Maui and that was the perfect plan. A couple of exciting days followed by 5 relaxing days. We would definitely stay at the Royal Hawaiian again. I felt like I had stepped back in time. One other thing... if you don't like pink, find another hotel. Everything (and I mean everything) is pink... sheets, carpet, towels, soap, napkins... even the grout between the tiles in the bathroom. This is a very charming hotel.

<Author>nikswrx
<Content>OK hotel, friendly staff...but there are better deals in Waikiki I stayed here for one night to cash in some of my Starwood Preferred Guest points. I wanted to stay at the Sheraton Moana Surfrider right down the street, but all they would offer me is a room with two twin beds, so instead I chose a garden view room here, with a king bed.All of the staff members were great. My boyfriend and I were greeted with fresh leis upon arrival. The front desk clerk was great, superb service! And we were able to check in early, which I wasn't expecting! The housekeepers always greeted you with an aloha and a smile as you walked to and from your room. Everyone there just really makes you feel welcome! We had a garden room in the historic, older section of the hotel. It was on the 4th floor, and looked out onto the valet area, which sounds bad but there are beautiful old trees and lots of greenery there so it actually seemed very serene. The hotel is set back from the busy street which means it is quieter here than the other hotels. (Even with the cars pulling in outside). We could hear the birds, and sometimes one would come sit on our window sill which was cute!There was also a loaf of banana bread and some jam set out for us, with a little card. A really nice touch!The room itself was....interesting. The bed is very high, and I am pretty tall (5'8) but I kind of had to climb up onto it. I could imagine this would be hard for older people, or short people. The ceiling was very high, which made the room seem very spacious. The bathroom was a generous size, and the pink towels were very soft and fluffy! (Usually I find hotel towels to be pretty thin and scratchy.)Yes, there are some small problems with the room....it does feel sort of old (e.g, the paint on the bathroom door was peeling) but since I live in a century old-home I don't find that sort of thing bothersome. I can appreciate the historic nature of this hotel.But for the rates this hotel charges, there are some things that they really should address. For one, the bed is not really comfortable, and the sheets and comforter seem like the same ones that you would see in a budget motel. Same with the tv...it was very tiny. Also, having a small fridge might have been nice. (We stayed in a less expensive hotel for another 3 nights in Waikiki, and it had a much more comfortable bed, 32 flat panel tv, and a fridge.)I would probably stay here again, mainly because of the friendly staff, and great location. But I just can't justify the price. You can get a much better deal in Waikiki.

<Author>nanicinema
<Content>Kind and Gracious Staff My family stayed at the Royal Hawaiian during a very difficult time - my mother was on her deathbed and doing home hospice and we couldn't stay at my parents house (who live in Honolulu). Needless to say we weren't into having a wild time in Waikiki. We wanted to be some place quiet and homey - a retreat from days spent saying good-bye to my mom - and therefore I immediately thought of the Royal Hawaiian. It had been my mother's favorite hotel in Honolulu since we moved there in the late 1960s. Only problem was that they were fully booked for a convention! However they managed to accomadate us - a miracle really - and gave us a very large suite in the old building. It was really quiet despite the convention. The hotel staff were kind beyond belief. At one point the front desk manager babysat my five year old daughter while I had to take care of an urgent matter. We stayed for over two weeks - so we really got to know the hotel and staff. It really felt like home during one of the worst times in my life. It's true the rooms need upgrading - but if you want quiet and charm in Waikiki this is it - everything else is boring. The beach is fantastic. It's not a Ritz or Four Seasons - so please don't expect that - but it is good for what it is - an old world hotel. And you're in the center of everything. I will always remember the staff's kindness. Mahalo.

<Author>TravelGirl1129
<Content>Royal Hawaiian is overrated We booked this hotel using Starwood points over the Moana Surfrider based on tripadvisor reviews. We were there in Late Jan 2007. We were looking for something with some more character than the standard high-rise hotels. However, I feel we would have been happier staying at the Moana Surfrider after all, or any other hotel on the beach. Check in was fine and the hotel has a lovely lobby, we were greeted with leis, and we managed to upgrade to an oceanrview room in the original building. We should have saved our points and stayed in a gardenview, as they was no lanai and, while the view was very nice and we LOVED listening to the hawaiian music from the band down at the Mai Tai Bar (the one night they played), it was a regular sized window, nothing special to justify the extra points (or $$, if paying). Other than that, we were fine with the room, while small, it was clean and somewhat charming, although definitely overpriced. I also read on their website that we recieve fresh banana bread in our room but we never received it. The bed was comfy. The room could have been more quiet, though, because the people next door were LOUD at all hours. We had an adjoining suite so maybe if it hadn't been connected it might have been quieter.They do have a nice beach but the beach/pool staff isn't terribly helpful. The location is great since it's central to a lot in Waikiki. One thing that really bugged us was they made us give up our chairs and towels before sunset and we really had planned to watch the sunset in our chairs. Basically, while we could have sat on the sand, we felt it was their way of forcing more people to the bar to pay a lot of $$ for drinks. So alas, we retired to the bar after all. Re: the Mai Tai Bar, it was fine during the day and early evening, but DEAD at night. Not sure if it was a weather issue (high winds when we were there) so we went to the bar at the Moana Surfrider which had a bit more going on, with a band despite the winds, etc. Lovely outside area at the Moana Surfrider with a huge banyan tree (just watch where you sit...you don't want a bird over you!)We had lunch a couple times at the Mai Tai Bar. While over-priced, the food was decent. Nothing special. Drinks were fine but a bit inconsistent, depending on who made them. Parking stinks because you have to park at the garage on the other side of the Sheraton WAikiki next door and finding it the first time was a bit confusing. They just need clearer signs, that's all. PROS:Central locationGroundsBeachCONS:ServiceCostParkingLast words - we had a very nice meal at the Ocean House restaurant at the Outrigger Reef hotel. Also, rent a car and drive the Island! Waikiki/Honolulu is like Los Angeles, outside of that city you get a better sense of real Hawaii. The island is small and completely driveable (you can forgo 4 wheel drive on Oahu.)

<Author>Bethannsd65
<Content>Awesome hotel, excellent service My husband has some business to attend to and I opted to tag along. I had a choice of several hotels, and chose the Royal Hawaiian on a whim, as it looked so interesting on its website. After booking it, I then went onto Trip Advisor and read the reviews. Needless to say, I had serious second thoughts and was very hesitant to stay here. I am so glad we did as we had an excellent stay. First of all, Glenn at check-in is professional and courteous. He was a pleasure to work with. We were greeted with a fresh Lei and treated wonderfully. Our Starwood Preferred Card was not able to be found in the system, and Glenn got it fixed, with no hassle and a minimum of time. He then upgraded us to a beautiful suite on the 5th floor. We were in the OLD tower. It was fine. The rooms were large, well decorated and clean. The decor was superb. The bed was comfy. There was a fridge and complimentary water daily. AC was perfect, we had a garden and slight ocean view. Nightly turn-down and chocolates on the pillows. The bathroom was small, but how long is anyone in there, anyhow? Our suite had a huge living room and we could have hosted a party for 50 people and had more than enough space. The beach is just outside, and we had no problems getting a chair and umbrella every morning. There was no horrendous line or crowds like we read about. We got chair side drink service on the beach. There is a little snack bar with burgers, etc right there as well. The food was pricy, but it's pricy all over Waikiki. The driveway to the hotel and the hotel itself is an oasis in the middle of such a busy city. The hotel is just tucked away and secluded. Incredible gardens and large trees. very lush and green, open and just a beautiful place. Stores (Louis Vuitton, my fav) are right across the street. The concierge was helpful and found us some great restaurants. We also went on a dolphin excursion and whale watching on a big (20 person or so) pontoon boat and snorkeled with the dolphins. Was great and worth the money. We booked that excursion through all hawaii tours on line.They picked us up on time, had a fresh fish lunch, and we saw dolphins and whales. This was a wonderful hotel and we would absolutely come back again. There were not many kids (and we left ours at home!). But it was Jan and not school vacation time. This is a great hotel and don't let the other negative reviews scare you off. A+++++++

<Author>bigredhouse
<Content>The Royal Hawaiian met expectations In November/December, we stayed at the Royal Hawaiian on our first night in Hawaii and our last three in a four-week 10th Anniversary trip. I read alot of reviews for Honolulu hotels and chose the Royal because it honestly seemed like the best of some fairly average hotels in our price range. We got basically what we expected: The tired rooms need renovation; the grounds and the lobby are beautiful; it's right in the middle of the action; the staff is fine although everyone seems to want to be tipped just for doing their jobs. A mix-up with our room took time and patience to resolve (the first was not the non-smoking requested but rather reeked of cigarette smoke; the second had not been cleaned (Housekeeping called later to try to return the jewellery that had been left behind by another guest to us!); the third was fine. The bellman who led us from room from room was great and the manager apologized with free buffet breakfasts, which was classy. He seemed sincerely diappointed with what had occurred, which is all a traveller asks for, right? Stay clear of the Mai Tai Bar if you want anything resembling good service. Our biggest learning would be to try to avoid Honolulu altogether - head out to Kauai, Maui, Heavenly Hana (stay overnight). Alan Wong's was the best restaurant in Honolulu - sit at the Chef's Counter for the best entertainment in town!

<Author>mince963
<Content>Mixed feelings My wife and I spent a weeks honeymoon at the Royal Hawaiian in October 2006 following our wedding in Las Vegas and a wonderful week of 5 star luxury. We were looking forward to a week of paradise after travelling half way around the globe. On arrival at the airport which is a concrete 70's monstrosity we arrived in Waikiki in the darkness and I have to say the high rise jungle was not what I had envisaged. The hotel itself was a pleasent suprise surrounded by exotic plants and burning torches lighting the way. It really looked impressive, a different experience for the usual modern concrete boxes. We were very disappointed not to be offered a flower lei on arrival by the staff as everyone else appeared to be wearing one and we wished to feel part of the cultural experience having never visited the islands before. Our travel agent had requested a honeymoon upgrade if available but none was forthcoming. We stressed the occasion to Bobby on check-in however he assured us that a fantastic room over looking the coconut grove had allready been reserved for us.Our garden view room was a shock to say the least and not of the nice variety. The room was dark with heavy floral wall paper, a very tired dark green carpet and a crack in the ceiling to rival anything we had seen in the Arizona desert. The view from the (no balcony) window was obstructed by a flat roof and directly opposite was the scaffolding adorning the building works on the shopping centre.The worst suprise was the bathroom which was miniscule, as pink as the exterior and with antique fittings.It goes without saying that there was no gift of wine, fruit or flowers to mark the occasion.On the plus side the bed was something special. I have never been as comfortable or slept as well.On a brighter note the location of the hotel and the pool area was great. The staff were friendly and we really enjoyed the pool and mai tai bars. Try the pink beer! We had a massage at the spa in the complex and it was wonderful if a little expensive.The surrounding area is a great experience, the Cheesecake Factory, Hula Grille and Coconut Willy's bar in the market.We were due to check out on the day of the quake and had to stay an extra three nights due to the cancelled flight.The staff were helpful and we were moved to another room which was a big improvement.( Obviously at our own expence ) We did get some free coffee and were able to buy a make do breakfast but other than that there was no other food all day. All in all we loved the island and would definatley return one day. The hotel was charming and after the initial suprise we did not regret staying there as it is worlds apart from anywhere we have stayed before and is like living in a 40's movie.I think the key is to look at some photo's of the rooms so you know what to expect and mybe be more vocal if you are not satisfied.

<Author>TheRealMC
<Content>We loved this hotel - what a great experience! We stayed at the Royal Hawaiian in December for 4 nights during a really busy time - the 65th anniversary of Pearl Harbor and the Honolulu Marathon were both taking place while we were there, and the hotel was completely sold out. Regardless, my husband and I were upgraded to an ocean-view room (from a garden-view) when we arrived.Granted, the rooms are a bit worn (minimally stained carpet, a slight tear in the wallpaper), but the ambiance and grounds of the hotel, as well as the staff, far exceed any minor details!As stated above, there were a few imperfections with the room. However, the bed was extremely comfortable (I think it was a Sheraton Sweet Sleeper bed) and our room was quite large. Our ocean view room in the historic wing did not have a balcony (but the windows did completely open). The hotel is absolutely beautiful and it is on the best stretch of Waikiki beach. The grounds are gorgeous - so lush and quiet - which is totally different from the scene in Honolulu and on Waikiki Beach.The hotel is in a great location, in the middle of everything. Our favorite place to eat was Duke's Canoe Club at the Outrigger hotel next door. Really good food any time of day, very reasonable, and a great ambiance.The Mai Tai bar is great. We had some fabulous mai tais that were quite strong and well worth the price. We ate at the seafood buffet in one of the hotel restaurants (I believe it's only on Friday nights, at about $50 per person) - it was definitely worth the $50 each and the food was excellent.What really made our stay at the Royal Hawaiian so special was the hospitality. All of the staff were so friendly and went out of their way to make us feel welcome. As previously stated, the hotel was completely sold out, yet the bell staff from one day to the next remembered us, where we were from, what we had done that day or the day before...and the only time we saw them was when we were leaving or entering through the lobby to retrieve or drop off our car. The housekeeper who was responsible for our room stayed past the normal cutoff for cleaning (3:00 PM) in order to clean our room, which we never asked her to do (we just assumed we had missed the cleaning for the day). The concierge was great with ideas and recommendations for what to do and when to go. The bartender at the Mai Tai Bar was fun and entertaining and made delicious strong drinks. All of the hotel staff we encountered were just wonderful - we can't say enough about them!We loved this hotel and definitely will be going back in the near future! What a fantastic experience!  
<Date>Jan 2, 2007

<Author>Girl_Lawyer
<Content>Best Choice, Given the Options I had great expectations for the Royal Hawaiian, as my parents and grandparents have always considered it the height of luxury on Waikiki. I did not want to stay in a high rise, but wanted to stay somewhere with a bit of history. My expectations were only partially met, however. The lobby and grounds were beautuful, and the location can't be beat. We woke up early every day and got lounges and umbrellas on the beach and swam before the beach got too crowded. The Royal Hawaiian truly has the best stretch of beach on Waikiki. We were also able to walk to the Hilton and several other hotels, and Duke's and the Hula Grill, next door, were convenient for meals. We did not eat at the Royal Hawaiian, other than appetizers at the bar, because we felt it was extremely overpriced. The Mai Tai bar was great for sunset cocktails, though, and the live entertainment was wonderful. It's also a good place to sit and enjoy the entertainment from the luau on Monday nights if you don't want to pay for the full luau experience.On the downside, the interior of the hotel just seemed a little... tired. I have stayed at much nicer and more well-kept luxury properties. Our garden view room in the historic wing was a disappointment. The carpet was old, it was dark, and the bathroom was tiny with dirty basins and horrible water pressure. I noticed that the rooms across the hall were much nicer, so apparently this varies.The service, too, was nothing special. The valets were helpful with directions, but some obviously expected a tip for doing little more than pointing us in the right direction. Maid service was not what I'd expect from a luxury property. We came back to the room for a quick shower just as the maid was entering, and she insisted on making us wait while she (hurriedly) cleaned our bathroom and room, rather than coming back later as we requested.Overall, I would stay here again, given the options. We got a great rate, however; I would not pay the advertised $300-450 rates to stay here.  
<Date>Nov 29, 2006

<Author>Sunnyhoney00
<Content>Local Says, 'Choose something else' As locals, we rarely get a chance to stay in Waikiki and play tourists. I've always wanted to stay at the Pink Hotel because it is such as famous landmark.The grounds and public spaces are gorgeous and awe inspiring of the true old Hawaiian way. At first blush, everything looks great.Then you notice that it is not a true 5 star property. It is a solid 3 star property, because of the beach access, and grand public areas.It falls short of a 5 star hotel because thestaff will point to where you will go, not take you there. They act like they are important, but really can't make the decisions to make small adjustments. (For instance, I asked about a late check out time the day before, and was told to call in the morning. I got the feeling the reception desk just couldn't be bothered. My promised Coconut Grove room turned out to be over the motor court, or as the front desk corrected me, porte cochere. The second room they gave me was wedged in between the administrative offices and overlooked the landscaper鈥檚 maintenance area. Finally, after personally consulting the guest relations manager, I was given the promised Coconut grove room.The furnishings are a bit worn and shabby. Light bulbs are weak, small bathrooms, with no counter space. Tables and flatware are a bit dirty, staffs clothing is not crisp and clean (especially at the mai-tai bar  restaurant). And the overall look is that it needs a good facelift and cleaning.Save your money, stay at a different Starwood property and you can still enjoy this hotel. The room charges are interchangeable.Even better, go to the Halekalani for a true resort, first class experience.

<Author>MML2006
<Content>Loved the Royal Hawaiian My mom and I took a girl's getaway trip to Hawaii last week and stayed at the Royal Hawaiian. My mom had always wanted to stay there and it definitely lived up to expectations. From the moment we checked in, we were impressed. We were moving from another hotel to the RH and walked over there about 9:00 a.m. just to see if we could start the check-in process. They greeted us with a lei and allowed us to check in. The room wasn't quite ready so they called housekeeping and asked them to rush our room. We went back at 11:00 with our luggage and they greeted us with another lei. After giving us our keys, one bellman escorted us to our room (giving us a tour along the way) while another brought up our bags. Everyone we met at the hotel was very friendly and went out of their way to help with whatever needs we had. We had a garden view room and it was perfect. We didn't need the ocean view since we were out on the beach most of the time anyway. The room was very comfortable and tastefully decorated. Affectionately known as the Pink Palace or Pink Lady it would be very easy to overdo it on the pink. There is a lot of pink in the hotel but it's done very tastefully and blends well with other colors. The closet was huge and contained an iron and board and a safe. The room also had a small refrigerator. That came in very handy.Food was expensive but that's to be expected at a luxury hotel in Hawaii. We enjoyed the Mai Tai Bar very much. It was very nice to sit out there and enjoy a drink and some appetizers right next to the beach. The mai tais were a little too strong but they had a lot of other tropical drinks that were wonderful.Before we checked out, the concierge allowed us to use the computer to print out our boarding passes for our flight home. The bellman also retrieved our luggage from our room and stored it during the day since our flight left so late.I was very impressed with every aspect of the Royal Hawaiian. The people were wonderful and the hotel was beautiful. It was everything my mom and I hoped it would be and I would absolutely stay there again.

In my opinion, an historic hotel, one of this caliber, guests should not be looking at multiple power cords running to an extension cord. All in all, LOVED the hotel-staff were great, location cannot be beat, grounds are beautiful. The room, hoever...

<Author>fweeb
<Content>Great for a quick vacation We found ourselves in the last gasps of summer vacation, needing a family getaway, so booked a week at the Royal Hawaiian. This was a first visit to the Islands for our girls (9 and 11). Although certainly a different experience than staying in Maui or the Big Island, we were charmed by the beautiful old hotel. We booked a ground level suite in the new tower. Our room looked out over the pool and ocean. The suite was wonderful, with the downstairs being a living room area and the upstairs a loft bedroom. The service was excellent and the staff very friendly and helpful. Of course, since the hotel was built in the 1920's, the pool area is small, but we didn't mind. The only annoying factor was the rush for beach chairs at sunrise. Rumor is that the trick is to generously tip the night before to avoid waiting in line. All in all, we enjoyed the retro experience immensely.
