<Author>Reminixpro1
<Content>Uninspiring, EXTREMELY overrated hotel A much anticipated but disappointing stay 23-30 July 2006. I'm a frequent traveler who truly enjoys a fine hotel, price being no matter if the quality and value of services is up to par. In this case, the Royal Hawaiian seriously failed in keeping to the standard. While doing a remodel in town, I booked the Royal for about 6 days over other Starwood properties at a rate of $295/night. Even though I'm a Starwood gold preferred member, I was promptly informed upon check in, that no preferred rooms were available, but that the newer, remodeled, Tower Wing rooms were available at $585/night. What constitutes a preferred room at the Royal Hawaiian, I still don't know. To its credit, the room we were assigned was large and spacious, towels and sheets were very pink and appeared new, and the pink rug in the bathroom was nice. Note, the sheets on the bed are deceptive. They use a very nice Egyptian cotton 300 tc top sheet on the bed while the fitted sheet is a standard 50/50 cotton/poly 180 tc. As for the heavenly bed, forget it. An old itchy blanket hidden between two pink sheets serves as a comforter. (Forget down comforters of the renowned heavenly beds) The springs on these beds allowed you to sink in and bounce around whenever you moved. The room had a commanding view of the rooftop, if you were to crawl out of the window. Everything in the room was dated, from the old school 1980s carpet, the cheesy, fake classical furniture, the pink flowered floor to ceiling WALLPAPER to the tiny 19 in RCA television! No minibar, while a miniscule college boy refrigerator served more as an electric cooler. Toiletries in the bathroom were a different story. Once again, the products were in old school Royal Hawaiian generic, brand bottles. While the bottles were large for hotel toiletries, you had to use at least half the bottle to suds up your hair. One can only assume that they are watering down the shampoo in the back. To make matters worse, we practically had to beg the housecleaning staff to get more soap and supplies after about 2 days. Toothbrushes were not replenished and forget about soap bars. I ended up leaving the toiletries behind at the end of the stay because they left nothing to be desired.Vaue wise, there is none. A hamburger from roomservice is $18.50 plus 15% plus $3.00 delivery plus .04166% tax. Meanwhile, just next door at the Sheraton (a much nicer hotel: see review) the cost is $14.50, etc. for the same burger in a brand new room with FLAT PANEL tv's on the wall. The buffet in the Surf Room is good, expensive at about $50 a head, but good, noneltheless. The Mai Tai Bar is an excellent place to watch the sunset and chill out but it too, at $9.50 a Mai Tai, is pretty expensive. The drinks are good and the service, depending on the server is good as well. Recreation wise, the pool is tiny, the guests arrive at 0700 to place their towels on the chairs and then leave them there all day. Only one or two pool attendants to serve drinks, etc. so service was slow at best. In addition to what is stated above a key disturbing fact about the Royal Hawaiian is that the staff there treats you as though you were doing them a favor by staying there. It was very disappointing, especially when paying $25/day to valet park and you tell them you'll be back in 30 min and they say, Sorry, bro, we have a big wedding in the hotel and have to park your car in the garage. Completely astounding. A final solution to this rant is that I recommend all readers wishing to stay at a Starwood property in Waikiki to stay at either the Sheraton or the Sheraton Moana Surfrider. Less cost for service, better service on the whole, better, nicer, completely remodeled rooms and a better feeling about the quality to value ratio.Bottom line: it doesn't matter how much you pay per night, all hotel guests who treat staffmembers and each other with courtesy and respect should receive a top quality room and unparalled service for the money they are spending.

<Author>kitdale
<Content>Hushed Elegance at the Royal Hawaiin We stayed at the Royal Hawaiian in July of 2006. When we arrived, we were upgraded from a garden suite to an ocean suite, Room #2 Oahu. It was on two floors, had two beds and two bathrooms and two televisions. The master bath was very large and had a jacuzzi tub. It had a lanai that overlooked the pool and the Pacific! The view was spectacular. The dining was also excellent although a bit expensive. The seafood buffet was wonderful - all the lobster, crab, oysters, shrimp and clams you could eat. Plus there were so many other dishes I can't remember them all. The luau was a bit expensive. Grab a seat in the Mai Tai Bar which is wonderful and watch the luau from a distance! Also, be sure to visit Duke's which is right next door. The Hau Tree Lanai at the New Otani Kaiman Beach Hotel is a great place for breakfast. Eat under the same tree overlooking Sans Souci Beach that Robert Louis Stevenson did. The nearby Cheesecake Factory is a good value, but it is very crowded. Go early.Be sure to park your car in the garage. It will cost $15 a day, but it is cheaper than the $25 valet parking. The concierge was very helpful. Rent a car if you have more than one guest; it is cheaper and faster. It is easy to get around once you master the one way streets!Be sure to go to Pearl Harbor to see the sights. Go early! I mean like 6:30 AM unless you want to spend the whole day there. The Iolani Palace and environs was interesting. The Dole Pineapple Planatation was okay but the drive to the north shore was more interesting. Go to Diamond Head and Hanauma Bay. The scenery on the windward side of the island is spectacular.We would sightsee most of the day and then return each afternoon to swim at the Waikiki Beach right in front of our hotel. Then we would enjoy a glass of wine overlooking the ocean on the porch of our room.We wish we had more than a week. I would return to this historical grand lady of a hotel anytime!

<Author>waverlywallflower
<Content>Nice to Stay There Once We stayed at the Royal Hawaiian in August 2005, celebrating our anniversary. The location is very good, but self-parking your vehicle is impossible -- you are forced to valet park (and at a steep charge too). There was a problem with our room when we arrived (they gave us a smoking room and I'm allergic to smoke), but they quickly moved us to another (non-smoking) room. Not much of a view from the room. We also learned that if you want to utilize the hotel's trademark pink striped umbrellas you have to get on a waiting list! Seemed a bit convoluted after the amount of money we paid for a room. The service was good and check out was easy and I do recommend staying there once since it does exude a certain charm.

<Author>OneTraveling
<Content>Needs a Re-Do This was a Starwood award stay for 3 nights. It was my 5th time returning to this hotel, so I knew what to expect. The hotel is showing its age in the public areas. The awnings were looking very worn and most everything else just seems to need a touch up.There are 2 sets of rooms - those in the Historic buidling (which are larger) and those in the Tower building (which are smaller but with a balcony and most have a nice view). We were offered a tower room for a charge, which we considered until we saw the room. It was Holiday / Hampton Inn quality at best, so we declined to upcharge.We were given an ocean front mini-suite in the Historic Building which was fine. Except that the bathrooms in the Historic building are tiny. No separate shower and just enough room to turn around in - not even sufficient room to leave toiletries in the bathroom.The furnishings were about the same in the Historic or Tower rooms. I have to say I was extremely disappointed with the Tower room we were shown. It was small and the furnishings were just in bad shape. I can't believe people pay extra for that building except for the balcony overlooking the ocean, which is a nice extra.The Historic Rooms are larger, but many do not have an ocean view. Still, I would choose these rooms over the Tower rooms as the garden views are quite nice at this property.Food is expensive and of medium quality. We never ate anything but breakfast and lunch - and both were good, but not great.Valet parking service is slow, so best not to be in too much of a hurry. Also, consider that construction is taking place on Lewers St which is a shortcut over to Ala Moana if you are going back toward the mall/Ward Center/Airport area. That can take 10 - 15 minutes to navigate through when they are working.The public areas are very charming - especially the gardens between the hotel and the shopping center.There are rumors that the hotel has been bought by someone who wants to completely refurbish the hotel to a true luxury resort. I find it hard to imagine how they can do that unless they completely reconfigure the rooms in the historic building to make the bathrooms larger, and possibly make the tower building all-suites taking 2 existing rooms and making them into one. Honolulu needs another luxury choice and this would be a nice property if it's done right.As it is, I would stay at this hotel again. In Honolulu, there aren't that many hotels that have a true beach front location with an actual beach adjoining the hotel. This one does, and for that I give it extra points.

<Author>Jamieagogo
<Content>The Best in Honolulu After spending 4 days in Maui at the Hyatt, it was wonderful to arrive here! Honolulu is hopping, you can walk everywhere, and it is so much more alive! And the Royal is at the center of everything. It was a relief to not have to pile into a van (there were 6 of us) to go some place, we could actually wander off alone and explore Honolulu. Such a break for my husband and I to escape our parents, trust me.Anyway, everything you hear about the Royal is true -with its grandness, elegance and old world charm. We were greeted with a lei by a thoughtful staff (and you can just tell they love working there) the quiet understated lobby is lovely; don鈥檛 miss hanging out on the veranda and the Mai Tai bar even with the $9.00 per drink price. Try to sip slowly鈥r have your coffee out there. There are breathtaking orchids throughout the lobby areas and displays of items such as the dresses worn to the opening night gala and photos of the impressive guests who attended. We had no problems at the pool or getting a place on the beach, the little snack bar poolside serves great salads made by the Surf Room at a fraction of the price, and after ordering, they brought it all the way out to the beach for us when it was ready.Stay in the old part if you are into the history, the pink rooms with high ceilings and individual furnishings were appreciated by us. The signature banana bread delivered to your room was nice and my parents did have a coffee maker in their room so ask if you want one. We chose to get it each morning from the coffee stations set up on each floor which I am pretty sure is better than any in-room coffee I ever had. One of the best things also is that you are off the strip, separated by the opulent grounds from the main drag so it is actually quiet there. A rarity on Waikiki Beach.We also went to the luau here, even though the reviews were not great, and it was perfect for us. I loved that it was right there, the food was wonderful and I am not a big on long shows anyway. It was fast and furious, with beautiful dancers and as corny as described in other reviews. But the food was really great and the desserts were to die for. It is like being at the most elegant party you can imagine. But if you want the authentic beach cove thing, may not be for you. This was a dress up affair with awesome ocean views. We had the best table, period. I think it is because we were a guest there, and also as a guest you automatically get a discount on the price. There is a 20% discount for this luau on the website for the Royal Hawaiian.We had dinner at the Surf Room on Friday night for the weekly Seafood Buffet and despite the $48 person price, loved it. Call ahead as a guest and ask for a great table and they will make it happen.Two tips: We made our reservations directly on the website and used the AAA discount - our rooms were $275 and I have never seen anything nearly that low anywhere else.Also, the website suggests taking a shuttle for the 3 Sheratons from the airport, which we did. However, the price to and from the airport in a cab or van is $25 so the $10 per person shuttle fare only makes sense if there are one or two in your party.

<Author>Teraza
<Content>It was ok... but not worth the money Since the first time i was in waikiki, about 7 years ago, I have always wanted to stay at the pink palace. I thought, wow, what a location! what a lobby! beaultiful. I want to sit on the prime property on waikiki beach, staring out at diamond head.I never really could see myself paying 350 US (im canadian) a night at a hotel. Im more of a 150-200 a night person. But finally i had enough starwood reward points (10,000 points a night - most starwood properties are more 3000-5000 a night) to stay for 2 nights. I was very excited.Maybe its because i just returned from the big island, or maybe its just because i didnt feel i was getting my money (points) worth, but i was dissapointed. When we arrived, there was no one there to greet us. We parked the car, went into the lobby and checked in. Check in was fine and they even let us check in early (12:30pm).THe bell men then came running after us (while still at the lobby desk) to grab my husbands car keys and figure out what we were doing. We said we would park the car ourselves... i didnt want to have to deal with a valet that seemed to not be around. and the rest of the time, it seems chaotic around there anyways. So, we went back to the car, removed our luggage and gave it to the bellman who seemed confused that we would park the car and then go to the room - but whatever. Oh and the welcoming lady found us and gave us lais and welcomed us to hawaii - which was nice.We parked the car - came back - they were good about seeing us return and getitng our bags to our room right away. After we tipped the bellman we got better service - but i dont like it when service depends on the tip - the tip should be the reward for the service. Anyways.the room was - like others have said - not up to par. Old furniture (i know its the look they are going for - but it could be nice old furniture and it isnt). There is barely any storage space for things and the desk for the computer was not sufficient. OH and they charge for internet access - at this price it should be included. AND they charge for local calls too (a buck a piece) at this price it should be included too.Bathroom and sundries are barely acceptable. No view in our room. No lanai. It was noisy. One robe. Poor bed linens. Stained carpet. Old, small tv, with not as many channels are other hotels/resorts.Maid service was good. they were good at figuring out when you were out and the room was made while you were gone. The banana bread was good and left for us promptly after we arrived. Hallways were impressive. The view was impressive too.They changed their regulations for reservation on the beach - for beach chairs. Now its first come first serve. Leave a towel on the chair you want. There are 3 rows of chairs, which i think is ok - but I would rather have 2 rows with better views and a reservation process. Instead we had to sit in the 3rd row because we didnt want to have to come down extra early just to throw a towel on a chair - seems silly to me.There were few attendants there and no bar service. They actually discouraged some patrons from having drinks on the beach - unbelievable. THey make you sign out towels but dont care if/when you return them. Seems silly too.The pool was cold and we couldnt swim in waikiki because of the sewage problems - very unfortunate, especially because i love the ocean. No service by the pool either.Check out was12:30 because we were starwood preffered guests -it could be 4pm if you were gold, but we werent. But we used their suite - which every guest had access to, to shower up and change later in the day. Because you fly out of honolulu so late, it makes the last day difficult without a room. Our bags were kept on the curb by the bellman until we left.There were actually very little frills to this place, taking into consideration the cost (even though i only spent points, hoping to find a place that would justify the cost so next time I would convince myself to pay these prices). Thumbs down - unfortunetely because i had such high hopes.  
<Date>Apr 23, 2006

<Author>golfclubgm
<Content>Beautiful Hotel... Can you say UPDATE? The Royal Hawaiin has all of the potential to be a world class hotel. Unfortunately, they fall short of the mark on overall value. If a night at the Royal was $200 I might expect poor bathroom sundries, old (small) television, no robe, 1 semi comfortable chair and low quality linen. However,... it's $500 a night! The setting and location are absolutely perfect. 80% of the staff get it and provide outstanding service. The grounds and common areas are beautiful. The mai tai's and food are great! It's the rooms! I just got back from a 4 night stay at the Royal Hawaiin and had a King Room in the Tower. The room description said recently renovated... Boy if they did... they should get a new designer or a bigger budget. The bathtub was old and sub par. They did have a removable showerhead... but it had very little pressure. Most $500 dollar a night rooms have a seperate tub and shower... nicer fixtures and upgraded ammenities. The Bed was nice but the linens were very sub par. Outdated bedspread and linen threadcount are unaceptable at $500 a night. Even if the location is perfect. If you are going to have one chair... make it a great one. (Check out the Park Hyatt in Chicago!) I talked to several guests who stayed in the historic side that the rooms were even worse. Some moved over to the Tower during their stay.Overall it was a nice stay... the staff and setting were very nice. However,.. on my next trip to Oahu... I would not stay at the Royal again. (Unless they got a MAJOR room facelift) I want to also flog all of the major hotel reviewers and applaud Tripadvisor. I found the professional reviewers to be way off the mark. It seems that they review off of canned press reports and don't actually stay at the places they review. I find Tripadvisor to be a very valuable place to find current, relevant reviews. Thank you fellow reviewers!

One room had a beautiful and comfortable king size bed and the other had a pullout couch and room enough for 2 rollaways in addition to the couch, so there was plenty of room for all of us. It had no view, but we didn't care. If you get a rollaway for a child call the hotel directly and ask them to fax you stating that the rollaway is at no charge - otherwise they might charge you for it. We booked the SPG35 rate which gave you 35% off the room rate and 35% off any of the meals that you ate in the hotel(or any of the Sheratons in Waikiki for that matter.) Whether you book that particular rate or not - kids under 12 always eat free with each paying adult if you eat the buffet at breakfast. With the discount we paid $341/night, which for what you got I felt was very fair. The hotel is absolutely gorgeous! It is such a quiet oasis from the hustle and bustle of Waikiki. The grounds are so lush and beautiful. The hotel itself is a grand old lady. It a classic and beautiful property that is meticulously maintained. Every staff member that we encountered was so pleasant and helpful - the hotel managers, the front desk and restaurant staff, the bellman in front, the chambermaids, to the concierge -they really treated you like family. We ate our breakfasts at The Surf Room restaurant in the hotel where the food was as outstanding as the view. The only negative I can think of was that if you like to do a load or two of laundry on your vacation (I do!) there are no laundry facilities. You can go to the Sheraton next door, but their laundry room was ridiculously crowded. There is construction going on at the Royal Hawaiian shopping center next door, but it had little or no effect on us. We have stayed at the Sheraton a few times before and the HHV, but The Royal Hawaiian has captured our hearts and we can't wait to visit again!  
<Date>Feb 25, 2006

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Needs updating quickly I have read all of the reviews and I can't tell you how disappoiinting the hotel is. They have not updated this place in at least 20 years. Okay, most of Waikiki has not been updated in 20+ years, but this hotel charges $400-$500 per night. Come on and at least put some money into the place. We checked into on the suites in the historic building. It was quoted at $1100 per night. As a Starwood Preferred Guest member, I received a better rate, but to my amazement, the room was something I could find at a comfort in. Cheap furniture than was chipped, peeling and falling apart. Stained furniture that is so outdated. The bathroom was also very tacky and old. The hotel reluctantly moved us to the tower suite. The suite had an amazing view and was a 360 degree turn from the first suite, but the furniture in the tower suite was awful too. Old, cheap and outdated. The location of the hotel is the best and the beach access is wonderful, but other than that, I would recommend anyone seeking a first-class hotel to look for another location or rent a condo.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>a grand old lady The historic wing is beautiful -- high ceilings, immaculate carpetting, wallpaper etc. Lots of detail in the paint and finishings, just strolling around the grounds and common areas was fun. Room large and spacious, TV and console area somewhat ordinary, bathroom small and pretty ordinary -- not much you can do with a bathroom built in 1927 -- but otherwise it was a delight to stay in a hotel so well kept and lovely. Staff very friendly, helpful and honest. (We accidentally left money out where it might have been mistaken for a tip and it remained untouched by housekeeping). Pool is small but why go in the pool when you have the best spot on the entire beach? Stay in the tower if you want a lanai. We received a $75 food and beverage gift for use in the bar and dining room, nice touch. If you get an invite to the manager's cocktail party be sure to go -- open bar, no selling and good food! We never felt crowded like you can in some of the really huge hotels. We'll be back for sure.

<Author>SkyeTraveler
<Content>A great hotel in need of some updating I'll preface this review by saying that I probably wouldn't stay anywhere else in Waikiki. The Royal Hawaiian has an air of history and elegance that no other Waikiki hotel can match. Its lobby, in particular, is airy and gracious, and it has the best location on the (very crowded) beach. The beachside bar is the best of any we've tried in Waikiki. That said, the rooms in the historic part of the hotel are in need of updating. (We've never stayed in the newer part, so can't comment on those rooms.) The bathrooms look like they're from the early 1980s, and all that pink just makes them look even more dated. Although I like the hotel's pink theme, I think that a more creative designer would have used it more sparingly and tastefully.If you can live with the faded -- but perfectly serviceable -- rooms, this hotel really is a gem. It always suggests old Waikiki to me, before all those tower blocks sprang up and mass tourism changed the whole character of the islands. If I could suggest an alternative hotel in Waikiki, I would. But none of the others has the romantic feel of this hotel.

<Author>ldtravel
<Content>A very nice hotel ........... This hotel is a beauty- even if you don't like pink much! The staff is very nice and the grounds are kept very well. Checking in was a bit weird because although the res was under my name they required ID from everyone in the room but that was not bad at all. The only problems I had were the following: The beach area was rather small so if their is a big group in town - you've got to get their early for a good spot. It is a public beach by the way. The Royal Hawaiian is an all smoking hotel -which means No non smoking rooms so my room smelled like cigarettes constantly - I am not a smoker so I did not like that at all. The staff tried to help by bringing in a huge deodorizer - that was nice but nothing. The A/C systems are very old and mine needed to be clean so the room was rather warm for the few days but after I called the front desk - they came in to clean it and that did the trick. They compensated us very well for this trouble- I must say. Above all -this is a beautiful hotel with the best Luau in town and it is perfectly situated for shopping and sites. I would stay again.Aloha!

<Author>EP
<Content>Lovely oasis in the middle of Waikiki We had our first stay at The Royal Hawaiian last month, and it certainly won't be our last. Had stayed during a business trip just next door, at The Outrigger, in July.What a difference in atmosphere! The Royal Hawaiian is much quieter with a lot more 'Aloha spirit' to it. (Now, we did have a fun time at The Outrigger with our business friends, but wouldn't pick it for a vacation for my husband and myself.)Returning to The Royal Hawaiian after day trips, or even just dinner down the street, was always such a pleasurable experience. Even though it is right in the midst of busy Waikiki, the simple act of strolling down the walkways from the street to get to your room makes you relax. Such a pretty place! Had a nice ocean view corner room with a wrap-around balcony. The room service came up exactly as we had ordered it, which we have found is almost a rarity these days! The pool and beach areas were clean and well tended to.We felt that we had the best of both island worlds...that of being right in the middle of bustling Waikiki when we wanted excitement, as well as having a calming oasis when we wanted to relax together.

<Author>lass=
<Content>Beautiful Historic Property I stayed at the Royal Hawaiian for my honeymoon. I really liked it. I had told myself all my life when I get married I'll honeymoon at the Royal Hawaiian. They put me on the Starwood Preferred floor, and sent me banana bread and champagne. The next night there was a man knocking on the door with loaves of banana bread, and he said they were welcome gifts for people who had just arrived. He asked me if I had just arrived today, and I lied so I could get another banana bread loaf. They also give you a lei of orchids when you check in. I was very pleased with the staff. There was a problem with the internet, and a girl named Avis apologized over and over and over... I was really surprised they were so humble. Most employees would just blow you off. You get a cheaper price on the Monday night Luau if you pay for it on your hotel room bill. Parking is $10 for self park, which is cheaper than a lot of other places. The beach in front of the Royal Hawaiian is probably the best because there are no rocks when you walk into the ocean. Every Friday night they have a seafood buffet. It was to die for, but the cost was $50 and each soda pop costs $3.50. You can rack up a high bill there. IF the Royal Hawaiian costs too much you'll love the Sheraton Moana Surfrider just 2 hotels away.

<Author>blade97
<Content>Enjoyed the Pink Palace My family of four with two small children traveled to the Royal Hawaiian in May 05. We had a wonderful time at this property. We booked two ocean view rooms, we brought my mother to watch the kids, and the rooms were great. We booked our rooms through Starwood Preferred Guest. Our rooms were located in the historic wing and had queen anne furniture. It was our 15th anniversary and the hotel had champagne waiting in our room on ice when we checked in. The bathrooms are a little dated but sufficient and the toiletries are nice. The bed is awesome. The windows actually open up to Waikiki beach and you can hear the music and ocean in the evenings. We really enjoyed the beach and the reserved chairs for guests. Make sure you reserve a day in advance. We had a great lunch and dinner at the terrace room and kids eat free. The pool is small but adequate becasue the beach is right there. The grounds are beautiful. It is a little difficult to find the hotel's parking but once your there the service was great. This is a classy hotel. The only real negative was we requested a late check out at 2:30 pm and they charged us an extra $25 per room. That is kind of cheesy for this level of hotel. Only stayed there 1 night for business and then on to Maui for more vacation but I can highly reccommend the Royal. It has the most charm of any of the hotels in Waikiki and was very romantic at night.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Perfect end to a perfect honeymoon The Royal Hawaiian, or shall I say the Pink Palace, was the perfect place to end our honeymoon. We arrived before check-in and were prepared to have to wait for our room to be ready but surprisingly the room was actually ready. However, they kindly offered us an upgrade if we were willing to wait a few more hours and to sweeten it they even offered free drinks at the Mai Tai Bar. They didn't have to ask us twice! We left our bags and went to climb Diamond Head which was spectacular. It was easy to spot the Pink Palace among the sea of hotels on Waikiki beach from up there. When we returned to the hotel our room was ready and waiting for us was a bottle of ros茅 champagne along with their signature banana bread, yum! Now, we knew in advance that we would be staying at the Pink Palace, but we did not realize that everything on the inside would be Pink as well! Even the shampoo and conditioner were pink! While some might think that is a little kitchy it perfectly suited the hotel and it's atmosphere. The Mai Tai Bar is great fun with live entertainment at night and beautiful sunsets right on the beach. It was neat to watch the surfers ride the waves until the last hint of the sun was gone. The Surf Room for breakfast was also quite good. The concierge was truly helpful with planning activities and meals. Turndown service was a nice touch. The Royal Hawaiian simply seemed magical and was the perfect way to end an amazing Hawaiian honeymoon.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Gentile and graceful pink lady If you are looking for a quiet location right on the beach, this is the hotel for you. It is somehow so secluded but within a one minute walk to the busiest part of Honolulu. The hotel is a gentile, pink old lady that has kept pace with modern times as you will see when you drive up to the open lanai, enter the elegant lobby and turn your eyes right to sweep down to the beach and view the ocean that is the most perfect 3 shades of blue. Sit for a few moments in the lobby and watch as the patrons arrive and glimpse the ocean for the first time with an open mouthed gape and always a smile. Ask for a garden view room in the older section where you will open your windows and look down to the palms into the picture perfect courtyard. Your friends will think you have suddenly returned home a professional photographer since there is not a bad camera angle in the hotel. Sure, the new wallpaper has a retro look taking you back into the earlier part of the century and the towels are pink but the beds are excellent and the maid service is great. It's all part of the charm. If you stay in your room there during the day you are missing out on what makes Honolulu so unigue. Eat breakfast at the hotel and you will get a table looking out on all the people that should not be wearing bathing suits, so focus on that perfect Diamondhead photo and the birds that peck among the tables, then relax and enjoy your meal. Get the fresh pineapple, slowly sip the coffee and so what if it is a little expensive, you are on vacation after all. Avoid the breakfast lines, which clear out by 1000 and don't go to the concierge when everyone else is heading there after breakfast and you will avoid all the crowds. The pool is small but who cares so hit the beach right off the pool. I would stay here again in a heartbeat so just relax, be polite and be aware as a tourist that you control your vacation so take the bad with the good and go with the flow of the islands.  
<Date>Jul 4, 2005

<Author>snowrefugees
<Content>A Classic Hawaiian Vacation! On our third visit to Hawaii, my wife and I finally decided to stay in Waikiki for part of our trip (we'd only seen it briefly on the last day of our honeymoon) before venturing to other islands. We could not have picked a better hotel! It was everything we wanted: luxurious, fantastic beach, friendly and helpful front desk and employees, only 6 stories tall for the most part, roomy, and generally everything you'd expect of of an impeccably maintained 1927 beachfront hotel. It still looks just as it did, but has been kept up to date with modern air conditioning and so forth. We slept great and had a great time! Our room's potential shortcomings (lack of a porch, garden view) didn't bother us a bit.The hotel does have some inevitable minor problems: because of it's age it has no garage; instead it shares garage space with one of the highrise boxes surrounding it. This causes a 5 minute walk from hotel to car. The restaurant was too expensive for us to even think about eating there, and the hotel shops were nondescript and overpriced (in this regard at least, the hotel blends right in with the rest of Waikiki). Also, since it IS in Waikiki, leaving the area to explore the rest of Oahu (which I highly recommend-Oahu has a lot to offer!) must take into account the traffic (if you plan right, as we did, you will see traffic jams heading towards you but not be caught in many yourself!). I can't imagine staying anywhere else if we are lucky enough to vacation in Waikiki again.  
<Date>Jun 27, 2005

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Shelter in Waikiki! This was my first trip to Oahu and coming from San Diego, I found Waikiki too much like home to feel as if I was 'on vacation. However, we could not have picked a better hotel. This hotel is an oasis in the boxy concrete jungle of all its surrounding neighbors. Yes, the rooms are smallish ( I though ours was quite generous and it was in the historic section) but the charm and professinalism of the staff more than made the experience wonderful. It still a Sheraton at its heart but you can feel the tradition and grandeur even today. The food at the Surf Room was not our favorite but we loved the Mai Tai bar and this hotel sits on the best section of the beach. We trekked to the neighboring hotels, including the posh Halekulani, and found ourselves coming back to the Pink Palace having decided we Definitely had picked the best property. Its not cheap to stay here, but its a whole different Waikiki experience thats worth the extra expense.

<Author>Layover
<Content>An Oasis I'll preface this by saying that I really hate Waikiki. The crowds. The noise. The over-commercialization. So when I was asked to fly in and speak at a conference, I was excited to visit the islands (I mean, c'mon) but was kind of dreading Waikiki. Wow. The Royal Hawaiian saved me. They put me in the older historic section. I've read a few reviews from people who didn't like it. Granted, they could have had a legitimately bad experience. Or, what I think is more likely, is that they were more accustomed to the box-like rooms that are standard here.My room is quiet. Outside in the garden birds are singing. The staff could NOT be more professional or courteous. Everything has been a 10. Surrounded by highrises and the insanity of tourism gone wild, this place is a fortress of solitude from all of that. I'll come back. In a heartbeat. And bring my family.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>The 'saving grace' of our trip! To make a long story short, we were to be on a 10 day cruise to Hawaii. Just before leaving, we learned that our cruise had been cancelled due to a problem with the ship's propulsion system. We planned our trip thru a travel agent in Hawaii with no research at all (VERY unlike me) due to the time limitations. We spent 5 nights in Maui and there were many circumstances which made our trip unpleasant. By the time we arrived in Oahu, we were quite discouraged, as our long-anticipated trip was not turning out to be what we had hoped for. Thankfully, we ended up at the Royal Hawaiian! If only we would have stayed there for the entire trip! The hotel is so lovely and grand. Everything is very well maintained. We were in a suite on the fourth floor of the main hotel (428 I believe). They wheeled in two nice twin beds to be arranged in the living room area for our two children. My husband and I had a separate room with a king bed. Both rooms provided TV's. The bathroom was not overly large, but well stocked with nice toiletries. All four of us were provided with cozy, pink robes (yes, they have kid-sized robes) and slippers. My 8 year old son , who is a total boy, even wore his! His sister had to wrestle him to the ground when I tried to take a photo of him in his pink robe. All of the staff, including housekeeping, was very gracious and accommodating. The hotel is situated on, in my opinion, the nicest part of Waikiki Beach with a beautiful view of Diamond Head in the background. Yes, this beach area is on the more crowded side, but it was never uncomfortable. We never had a problem securing beach chairs. Note: we stayed five nights..April 2-6th. This is not considered the high season. The kids participated in two days of surf lessons and had a ball! It is easy to secure instructors at your convenience, as there are many located along Waikiki Beach. As far as dining, we did not eat at the hotel other than at the beachside cafe at the pool area (the pool area is not very large if you are looking for this feature). The cafe was good..of course, high priced as well. We enjoyed walking to several area restaurants which were considered a little more reasonably priced. We loved Duke's Canoe Club and the Ocean House. We also went to the Cheesecake Factory which was next to the hotel. The Royal Hawaiian is in a wonderful location to shopping and dining...you can get just about anything you wish. The shopping is also fantastic. We chose to self-park which saved some money and was no problem at all. I did have to go next door to the Sheraton Waikiki to use their workout facilities, but it really was no problem and the gym was well-equipped. We would definitely return to this hotel!  
<Date>May 3, 2005

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Loved the location of the Royal Hawaiin We stayed a week at the Royal Hawaiin from January 4th 2005. We had a room on the ocean front except the last night because all ocean front rooms had been booked previously. We loved the ocean front view! I could wave at my husband and child playing on the beach from the balcony. It was like having the ocean and the palm trees right in my backyard. Although it was much more expensive than the garden view room, it was well worth it. The ocean front rooms are also much newer. I had a couple of minor problems staying there. On one night there was a footprint on my pillowcase and on another a hole in my sheet. It was hard to believe this could happen there. I had them change the sheets but didn't complain about it because I didn't want to get anyone in trouble. I was a little annoyed when I could not get any prices from the concierge and when she told me she would have to get back to me. I guess it is not classy to have brochures with prices in the hotel. I complained at the desk and the employee told me it was just a misunderstanding. After all this waste of my time, I realised that these brochures and great coupons for activities and actractions are available on Kalakaua Ave. I sent my husband to the concierge to rent a car and it took a long time for the concierge to get back to him. The concierges were just swamped. However, I think that the Royal Hawaiin is the prettiest hotel in Oahu, the location is the best, the staff is nice and the ocean view is breathtaking. It also means a lot to me to stay in a place that is rich with History.

<Content>Love the Pink Lady I am astonished at the negative reviews of this wonderful hotel, the classiest place in the whole of the Pacific with a reputation going back to the twenties. This hotel has a charm, an aura that is unsurpassed. <Content>Cant wait to go back! We stayed at the Royal just a short time in April of 2005 at the end of our trip, but loved every minute of it. The hotel is gorgous and very inviting. The hotel staff is friendly, informative and very helpful. We stayed in the historic wing of the hotel with a garden view which was very nice and fairly large. The pool is not huge but large enough to share, very clean and the chairs under unbrellas are a great retreat from the hot sun of hawaii. The food was fantastic - we ate at the hotels seafood buffet they hold on Friday nights, and the wait staff was again friendly, fun and first class all the way. We also treated ourselves to the hotels Spa for a couples massage. It was heavenly. We fell in love with the Royal Hawaiian, Oahu and the people who take pride in where they work and live. We will definatly be back again.

The rooms are elegant and charming with the highest ceilings and the most wonderful hand carved doors. When we checked into our room we received the most wonderful platter of fruits, nuts and banana bread and a fantastic display of fresh flowers. We love the pink, the private beach, the whole opulent feel of the hotel. Most importantly the staff were very friendly and polite and the concierge can't do enough for you. We had our three children in a room next door to us and it was a truely magical experience for them. They loved sitting out on the beach in their own private area. We will definately stay at our favouite Hawaiian hotel again.  
<Date>Apr 3, 2005

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>The best! Our family just returned from a wonderful stay at the Royal Hawaiian, where we have stayed many times before. The ocean view luxury rooms are large, with expansive views of Waikiki beach and the hotel luau if you are there the right night. You do pay more for these rooms, but it is well worth it. The hotel's private roped off beach section has wonderful soft white sand and is a great place to people watch. The hotel staff could not be more warm and reflective of Hawaii's aloha spirit. Breakfast and lunch are quite edible, although we would not recommend eating dinner at the hotel (check out Alan Wong for a great meal). We will continue to return to the Royal with enthusiasm.

<Author>NovatoTraveler
<Content>Great Hotel, Remember this is Waikiki! My husband and I stayed at the Royal Hawaiian 2/21/05 - 2/27/05. I was nervous about the hotel after reading the reviews here. We were very pleased. First of all, this is Waikiki. You are not going to find a hotel on Waikiki with a better pool or set up. Royal Hawaiian has a private beach as well. They also have a great pool/beach reservation policy so you don't have to fight the crowds early in the morning to get a beach or pool lounge. The location is fabulous. You are right in the midst of Waikiki, can walk everywhere and right on the best stretch of beach. The staff is very friendly and the place has class and elegance that the new resorts and hotels lack today. The rooms have very nice furniture. The wall paper is dated but who cares about wall paper? The bathrooms are dated. I am someone that this normally really bothers but the elegance and class of the room makes up for it. The location, the private beach, the staff, the pool and bar, and the grounds all make this a great choice. If you are looking for a nice hotel right on Waikiki beach in a great location, I think you will be pleased.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Quit Whining My gosh, I get tired of hearing people whining about the Royal Hawaiian Hotel.! It is a wonderful hotel, with great rooms, a great location, and great employees. I stayed for 5 nights on June 2004 and thoroughly enjoyed it. This is a 100% classy hotel.Make no mistake about it, it is an expensive hotel. All of the people who complain about the rooms did it to themselves. Instead of reading I got a garden view room... you should read I went as cheap as possible.... If you went on a cruise and stayed in a room just above the engine room to save money, should you complain because you did not have a beautiful view? I think not.Go and spend the bucks. Do not stay in the new tower wing. The Royal is known for it's history, so stay in the historical part of the hotel. Spring for the Royal Ocean View rooms, you will not regret it. Sure there is no balcony, the hotel was built in 1927 for Christ sake, no hotels had them at that time. Accept the hotel for what it is and enjoy. Enjoy the real wood furniture, the hand carved doors, and the four poster beds.I cannot vouch for the food. It was expensive so I went elsewhere to eat. But my wife and I did try their Mai Tai's and pink beer (yes, everything is pink there).Starwood (Sheraton, manager of the Royal) has many promos. When I stayed there I got 35% off and got the 5th night free. The room was less than $300 a night for a great room with a real walk in closet and a great view of the luau. I paid more money before in Hawaii for a much lesser room.True, I wish that the shopping center had not been built to hide it from Kalakaua, but that is unavoidable. In fact, there are some benefits as it shades the hotel from the noise of the busy city just a few yards away. The landscaping was done so that, for the mosy part, you think that you are in an isolated oasis in paradise.So many famous people have stayed there, you can just feel the history. True, fame is fickle and has moved on to newer digs, but these other hotels are not better, just newer.I have no vested interest in the hotel, other than being a VERY happy customer. I am saving my frequent flyer miles and nickles to return asap.  
<Date>Feb 15, 2005

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Pink Palace Party ??? After traveling 5 1/2 hours first class, taking a limo to the hotel, we were ready to ho ke lau and party. 13 of us arrived to a hotel that had lost it's glory many years ago. The accomodations were unacceptable. No one in our party received the rooms they were satisfied with. We were moved 3 times, Our first room, in the historic section was adequately sized, but the sofa was so dirty, that you couldn't sit down. The bathroom had burn marks on the counters and tub, straight out of aBmovie!, and the carpeting was smelly and worn. Then the hotel upgraded us to their junior suite! Complete with no air conditioning, the same dirty sofa( must have been a matched set!), and a dorm room refrigerator (stuck in the middle of the floor ) as furniture!! The 3rd room was in the newer tower. Although much smaller, it did have an ocean view, so we stayed put. Our compadres fared no better in their search for rooms! Each ended up moving multiple times. The hotel , although majestic to look at, with huge potential!, appears to have no on-site management present. Operated under the Sheraton Starwood program, we were told that a Mr. Randy Ha was the General Manager, and worked out of the neighboring Sheraton hotel. If that is true, we never were able to make contact with him/her. Funny story, we were all invited to a cocktail party hosted by the manager, but no manager(s) were present. Additionally, there is only 1 restaurant in service at the hotel. It is buffet styled, poorly serviced, and dirty. We ended up spending our food dollars at the Halekulani hotel nearby. Although the day to day staff was courteous and helpful, this hotel needs a management overhaul. <Author>queeney2
<Content>Just Elegant !! My review is a little late but Here goes. We stayed at the Royal Hawaiian 11/19-11/24/2004 and our stay was nothing but pleasant. Upon arrival we were greeted with beautiful lei's and a warm Hawaiian welcome. Our front desk clerk told us that if there was anything that was not acceptable (good) to notify the front desk immediately and it would be taken care of, she said our staisfaction was their goal. Well I was satisfied all week. The room was old, yet elegant, I would not say it was outdated. Keep in mind this really was a palace!! Each room in the historic wing is a littlee different. Yes, as I read in other reviews you do have to reserve your beach/pool chaises for the next day. but if you go down @10:00 w.o. a reservation they give you what is not reserved. This was one of the nicest amenites! Each day I said where I wanted to sit, pool or beach, front or back, etc.. and my chaise was ready with plenty of towels. At the neighboring hotels you have to rent your umbrellas, chairs for the beach(not pool), and many make you accountable for your towels, not here. Not to mention the largest and nicest beach on wakiki. I walked from one end to the other form sand that is primarly hard rocks to a 20 ft beach.But that is not what makes this the Pink Princess, it is the staff. I can not tell you how customer service oriented this hotel is. The valets giving maps with directions highlighted, telling us things to watch out for and great beaches to go to. The room service delivering my 16yo old son the famous banana nut bread to the lobby . The front desk giving him a going away lei because he gave to someone who did not get one at another hotel. These and many other things that I could babble about some more make this hotel the spiit of Aloha. Queeney

<Author>Hawaiiantaco
<Content>The Pink Palace We just returned from a trip to Hawaii. Although we have been to several Hawaiian islands, this was our first visit to Oahu. We stayed at the famous Royal Hawaiian Hotel. The building is quite impressive. It is expansive, decorative, historic, and very clean. Diamondhead is an easy walk along the beach. The staff is courteous, friendly, and willing to help. The hotel has beautiful gardens and a large botanical area which encompasses a lawn area. While we were there, we saw a wedding performed on the lawn, as well as a hula contest. The location of the property is convenient to shopping and restaurants. Waikiki Beach is beautiful and the hotel has a great beachside restaurant. Although the costs are at times prohibitive, the amenities are wonderful. Be prepared to spend $15.00 a day for valet parking. Without the valet service, parking is $10.00 a day, and the garage is not all that convenient. This is a great place to spend some time. Our visit to Oahu, and the Royal Hawaiian, was diminished somewhat as a result of the sheer numbers of people we encountered! The beach was crowded, the shops were crowded, and the traffic was unbelievable! Before arranging to visit the area, you might want to do some research. We found the West side of this island far less busy.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Romantic, but lacking service My wife and I just returned from our honeymoon in Hawaii. We spent the first few days in the Waikiki area at the Royal Hawaiian hotel. We wanted a place that was a little more romantic and nostalgic than the usual beach hotel. The Royal Hawaiian fit the bill perfectly as our suite overlooked the beach area and included antique furniture, etc. As perfect as our room was, the service from the majority of the employees was Holiday Inn caliber. From the moment we checked in (which took over 20 minutes - and we were 2nd in line!), we found the staff at the front desk to be less than helpful and completely inattentive. Since we were not able to find a concierge in the hotel, I was left to assume that the front desk must usually handle questions about the area. So a word of advice - do your own homework before getting there. I am glad that I had so that I didn't need to rely on their rude, unhelpful behavior.

<Author>lass=
<Content>Terrific! Stayed here for 3 nights in March - also stayed a week in nearby Moana Surfrider (see seperate review). This hotel is just great. The olde-worlde atmosphere just oozes from the walls. We found the hotel to be in a good state of repair and we had a reasonable-sized room in the original hotel building. The pink bathrobes, towels and toiletries; the pink umbrellas you sit beneath to sip your Mai Tais whilst you listen to the sound of crashing surf and live Hawiian music - this is the stuff dream holidays are made of. Both Starwood properties have an excellent location right in the heart of Waikiki and fronting the beach. A plethora of shops and restaurants are right outside your door. On two occasions during our stay we found ourselves swimming with giant sea turtles right next to the hotel and the busy beach! Just amazing. If you have any doubts about staying, or have any specific queries before making up your mind then e-mail me.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>The Pink Palace is classic in every sense of the wors I have recently stayed at the Royal Hawaiian, and I personally think it is still a class act. And, judging by some of the comments made on this site, many people share seem to share my opinion. For those of you who had a less than perfect stay, I can only wonder about the attitudes and perspectives of those who posted less than kind comments. Yes, this is a well established hotel which was built during a time when rooms were sized smaller, and hotels where built without lanai. And it's also true that the elaborate gardens and grounds of the Royal were gobbled up by greedy investors, so that the Pink Palace is no hemmed in by massive concrete structures. But all of that hasn't detracted from its aloha spirit, or the gracious service of its staff, or the most desirable beach front location in Waikiki. It is difficult for hotel management to schedule repairs and renovations during high season when the hotel is booked to capacity, so hotels are forced to take care of less serious matters during off peak seasons. This includes the Royal Hawaiian, whose shocking pink facade is repainted, without fail, every 5 years. In closing, I would like to say that you really get what you pay for, so if you book online with a discount broker for a cheaper than cheap price, don't be disillusioned into thinking you'll have an ocean front penthouse suite upon checkin. But if you are courtesous(read that not demanding), you might get upgraded a category or two, if it is available. Aloha e mahalo!  
<Date>Mar 21, 2004

<Author>Ralph1955
<Content>Charming Old Waikiki I toured the Royal Hawaiian as part of a travel agent fam in March 2003. I was very impressed with the preservation of this historic landmark. I had always pictured it in my mind to be nothing but a gaudy pink resort. I'm pleased to say I was proven wrong! The color scheme is more of a coral and it blends with the ocean and sand very well. What impressed me most was the hand carved wooden doors of the old part of the hotel. Each guest room has its own decorated door that really sets the tone for elegant charm. I actually preferred the garden view rooms over the ocean view because it gives you a totally different experience. Honolulu is right outside your door, but with the excellent landscaping you dont feel like you are in a city. We saw the gardens dressed up for a wedding and witnessed the happy couple having their portraits taken afterwards. Absolutely breathtaking. This is the perfect place to begin a cruise package around the islands or a honeymoon. Highly recommended!

<Author>meems_cat_2004
<Content>Treated "Royally" at The Royal Just returned from a 10 day trip to Hawaii. Spent our first four days in Waikiki at The Royal Hawaiian. We were upgraded at no extra cost to a 12th floor ocean front room in the tower with a marvelous lanai. Lei greeting.....my daughter at first chose a candy lei and then when she saw how lovely the flower lei ws she wanted to trade.......the desk clerk simply gave her the flower lei in addition. This was an example of the superb service we received the entire stay. Though we didn't eat at the hotel a lot, the meals we did have, mostly breakfasts were very good and the room service was quite prompt. Everyone from maids to valet to front desk people were extremely polite and eager to please. When we ate Sunday breakfast, my daughter's meal was free, another nice surprise. The pool is not large but pleasant and right off the beach which we could access by stepping out of the elevator, down a couple of steps and there you are. Finding lounge chairs on the beach did not seem to be a problem and we never had to reserve one. There were a lot of Japenese tourists there, so I felt almost like I was in Japan, but having visited there before I did not mind. Mostly people were very polite. There is a wonderful ambience to this place which does hearken back to a bygone era of luxury. The garden is not large but still very lovely. The parking valets were very attentive and prompt, also helpful with directions when needed. There is a daily parking fee which most hotels charge......but the convenience of valet parking made it worthwhile. The nightly turndown service was a very nice touch and my daughter especially enjoyed the chocolates on our pillows.We walked over the the next door Sheraton Waikiki for Sunday breakfast and it was very noisy and busy in the huge lobby.........we turned around and came back to the Royal where we appreciated the more quiet atmosphere and enjoyed a very lovely breakfast with a marvelous view of Diamond Head and the beach just outside.The only downside was that toward the end of our stay, renovation on the tower unit forced the closing of one of the elevators which was slightly inconvenient and lengthened the wait to go up and down. This should be done soon however and the newly rennovated rooms are very nice......ours being one of them.It was my daugher's first trip to Hawaii and will always be a memorable time for us both. It was enhanced in large part by the wonderful staff of this grand old hotel. Others may be looking for something else, but this is exactly what we had hoped for and more. We would come back here again!
